O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You dear children, I have completed this book which is the culmination of the science of medicine, bringing together its completion through my explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in vision that I would complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is well established in our region and has spread everywhere, it has lost its science and been divided up, and nothing remains from it except for small descriptions in books written by the ancients that were handled by hands.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And because of this, there has come error and vanity, and closed are the minds, and the science is far away.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems that I should revive this treatise together with the order of its content according to the path of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and come together in assembly the forms of the cautery irons, and the other tools of work along with the adjustment of declaration and preparation of them, as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no good masters are found in our times, the art of medicine has been neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he who intervenes should ascend in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so long as they know how to judge members, and their forms and connections and separations, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and muscles, and the number of bones, and their movement and the moving and resting veins, and where their exit lies.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And thus, according to Hippocrates, he says that without knowledge it is little, and with practice it grows some; similarly in the art of hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We shall tell you at the start of this book that if someone lacks knowledge about what has been discussed, they may easily commit errors and mislead others; just as I have seen many times among those who interfere with this science and abandon their knowledge and lack of experimentation.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a fool who tried to cure one of the scrofulous swellings or neck of a woman. He tied off the arteries below her neck; so much blood flowed out that the woman died in his hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I saw another fool who was treating a stone in an old man's body, and the stone was large; he took along with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have already been called to extract, and saw the position of the organ and the size of the stone, and indeed if they had cut him he would have died.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And saw another case where I treated the leg of a Duke from our land, who had broken his leg and sustained an injury due to the breakage. The surgeons ignorant tied the break over the wound, causing inflammation there; they didn't stop with the treatment till it improved after one week; then instructed not to disassemble it again; so waited until the leg was fully swollen up and down and eventually led to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I have been summoned to help him, and I hurried to free his leg. And when I found it dislocated so perfectly, he was in peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But every path of corruption had already been confirmed throughout the body or member, and there was no way to heal it; and the corruption continued to spread within the body until the entire member was lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And there is another method that collapses an abscessed wound, and then inflames it through the wickedness of her lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a chancre, when it is full of melancholic humor, it should not be touched with iron if it cannot all be removed, what has been corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And because of this, dear children, you are required to know that the work of hands is divided into two parts: meaning, those situations where there are risks in multiple positions. And I will show each one in this book where there is danger and risk.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Because it is necessary for you to take care of this, so that no one may speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	If you prepare your weapons carefully, and treat your illnesses gently yet firmly, and use the best approach so that through God's grace you achieve salvation and become whole; and leave behind terrifying diseases with no complaint of health; and remove from yourself those who cause doubt, and have faith in what you can do so that you may go from this world to glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»	Galien mentions in some of his admonishments: "Do not treat illnesses improperly, lest you be called foolish by the people."
J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc .iij. chapitres.	I have composed this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters deal with fire cauteries and medicinal cauteries, and the chapters are organized from head to bones; and about the forms of instruments, and the materials for cautery tools, and all that is necessary in work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapters are about cutting and piercing, and suction cups and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and the chapters are organized and contain the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapters deal with restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; it is organized from head to bones, and includes the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Just as we remember our work, it is necessary for me to tell you about the quality of each remedy and its harm associated with each temperament.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of aid, and harm, are the longest word and most subtle science and the secrets respond; and many wise people spoke about this, agreeing with it. And they were content with their words for me, because I fear its length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the fire cautery universally benefits all compositions where there is substance, because it caters to two types of composition: these being known as warm composition with substance, and dry composition with substance.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In the warm and dry combined with substance, there was no agreement and they said that the fire cautery is great help; and another group said the opposite: that the fire cautery only benefits illnesses caused by heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is so hot, and should never be treated with hot diseases through heat or drying. And this person who says the opposite, that the cautery provides great help to hot and dry illnesses that come into people's bodies.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of the person and their moisture to the aspect of fire, you find that the body is cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it true on every occasion by experiment.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And for every way, do not intervene except that which has been proven and by long use known, the art of cauteries, and the diversity of skin types, and the dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the occurrences and duration; we have no fear from other skin types, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the instruments gathered together with the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	Know, children, that when a fire cautery is assembled, it contains the secrets of healing, and offers more benefit than a burning medical treatment.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not come forth from any member except that which is cooked, and it harms no other member if you do not name it.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	Hot medicines spread from one part of the body to another when they are removed, causing diseases and disorders in various parts of the body. And by chance, they might cause trouble for the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire by its height and by the goodness of its nature does not do this if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found for you through experimentation and from the longevity of my service and study in the art, it is true about things; and for this reason I apologize for the length of speech, because I do not want to withhold the secret that has been revealed regarding fire and its quality, how it relieves diseases in the body, as the philosopher explains by demonstrating. May you accept these insights in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, child, that they agreed on when the cauterizations should be done, and read prayers.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is suitable in all times, because the nuisances happening are mitigated by the help of the cautery; and indeed, if the cauterizations are for necessary pains greater than can wait until larger mischief befalls the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think of it, little child, as the foolish people do; for a disease cured by cauterization does not have recurrence. And they say it like this: but it is not quite as they believe, because cauterizations are only medicine that changes complexion and dries the fluids which cause pain, and is worth more than medicine due to its speed in enhancing valor, and due to the virtue of its work and authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And know that when disease comes, it happens according to the complexion of the sick person and the location of the disease and its virtue; and there are gathered in him the excesses due to the consumption of meats and similar things. If only cauterizations were administered where there is little excess and moisture, such as cauterizations for pain, and similar things, then that kind of pain does not recur; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And no one understands why cauterizations are called the later ones in medicine, and this is seen; but they do not believe that cauterization holds after medicine. But their understanding is false, and cauterization is considered the later ones of medicine because when we administer our healing methods in any disease and they do not work, then we administer the cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, it is correctly understood that cauterization belongs to the later stages of medicine, not according to the understanding of those who misunderstand.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The old ones said that cauterizations made from gold instruments are better than those made of iron, and they said this only due to the quality of gold and the purity of its substance; they also stated that the gold parts of a cautery do not cause ulcers, but that is not true as I have proven it myself, and found out that this is indeed true in some individuals; and cauterizations made with gold are better than those made of iron, just as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet, when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not realize it by the color of the gold, and it is suddenly cooled down; and if you heat it too much; they place it in fire; and thus there is enough prevention.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And because we use our metal cautery that has been adapted to our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	So I have organized this chapter on the shoulder until this point, so that finding it may be easier.
dou cautere olivaire	The olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	A fire cautery is suitable for moisture and coldness on the head. There are two kinds that we do this due to the cause of an illness called 'soda', and because of many fluids that descend from the body like sweat, and from ears, and through a multitude of dreams and toothache and sore throat, and also towards all diseases that come from cold such as paralysis, soda poisoning and apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The shape of this cautery is such that the body's maladies are purified by a dissolving medicine altering the head. Three times or four times, according to how the virtues and the acidity and the habituation of the malady can bear it; and then you should reapply over the head of the malady.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then place his palms together, and position your hands on the sides of his nose; after that, place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two nostrils; and let it be where your middle fingers go, if it bleeds from there, then heat up the cautery which is called "olivare", whose form is as follows:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	Apply ink to his shoulder mark, and while descending and stretching your hand gradually and steadily, move it back and forth. Then lift your hand alone, checking if you see the bone. If you don't see it, continue with the cautery until you do see the bone as I've instructed; afterwards take one part of charcoal, place a moistened soft cotton inside, put it on the shoulder mark, and leave there for three days. After that, apply a poultice made from butter onto it; let it remain until the scorching disappears; thereafter treat the wound with ointment known as 'tetrafarmaçon', until it heals properly.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And if they said among the old ones that when a wound remains open for longer, it purges more; and because of this advice, they moved.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And it was said by some that one should let the cautery burn until part of the bone is burned, and then remove what has been burned from the bone and treat it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And they say that concerning the cautery one must allow it to stay there and press so strongly that you raise as wide of an area around the bone as would be made by a single ellipse, like what women place in their needles when menstruating because the body fluids are forced out; and should one leave the wound open for a long time after that. Afterward, one must clean it and stitch it up.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cautery do not seem to me to be good for everything, except where there is a passage for fear; and I think that I should allow them. Because the joints become weakened by continuous exposure to nature's solutions, as we have shown in other limbs, and even when the joints are weak due to nature itself, my first impression of cautery is more healing and stronger for me, and from this method I work together with it thus gathering health.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the old pain in the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When throughout the entire head comes chronic pain and lasts long, one should use the patient's years of experience and pills which are called "cochies", and treatments for clearing the head and ears and bandages; and if one applies the cautery as we have previously mentioned, it is effective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care that the shoulder of the patient is of strong nature and not too cold; therefore, apply the cautery just below this cautery as we have explained above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After you have done the cautery on each of the joints up to the bone as we said before, and do another cautery at the place which is called 'vassel'; and attach two levers where suction cups are placed; and lift your hand so that you cannot touch the bone: the patient feels much more pain in this cautery than in others, and I will explain further. And it must be that the cauteries on the joints are finer than the one used for half of the head, and they should have this shape:
dou cautere dou chief	For the fire cautery,
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain comes to part of the head,
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The medicine-cautery if you take one spoonful of oil,
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the ointment treatment as long as it is clean; and if you see fit to use some burning medicines that I have written about or the tenth treatise on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere. Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	The iron cautery is done in this manner. Heat up the form of the cautery as described:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And call it "closed" because its head is made in the shape of a bell with a .i. point of curvature, and in the middle there's a small appearance; and place it on the painful area, hold your hand and gently move the iron for a bit until half of the edge of the wound is burned; then lift your hand to prevent the artery from burning, it is done, and allow an abundance of blood to flow.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After putting on sailcloth and place it on the wound for .iij. days; then remove it and apply wet cotton soaked in butter, then continue treating the wound with ointment until it is clean; and if you wish to cauterize this headache with the cautery that is called "cultellare", do it at the tip only, and be careful not to cover the artery in this headache which is not old.
de emigraine	From headache
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat headache as we have described before in the divisions of diseases, and it doesn't improve, and when the fire cauterization tools which were discussed earlier are tried on metal but do not adhere, then it is necessary that you heat up the "cultellare" type cauterizing tool until it becomes white; and so with your hand guiding along a line half the length of its full size from the elbow, apply once while making sure not to cut the artery and stopping just before reaching the bone; and be careful not to let the jaw move when eating, making sure only the gum is in contact without causing spasms in the patient, and guard against bleeding from the artery if it is cut or severed even with fear and likewise for those who are unaware of this and have not been trained and experienced; leave the work halfway done; but I will tell you how to stop bleeding when the artery is cut, and show you where it is mentioned in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauterizing tools do not adhere to the disease, and patients are suffering, cauterize them in the middle of the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it heals; and when you observe this, administer the cauterizer that we have mentioned or in the chapter on the extraction of arteries, with a cauterizer having two knives; and these cauterizers are better than others and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	From the pain of the ears from coldness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain in the ear comes from cold, and one has applied solutions of medicines and other treatments that we have mentioned under division, and if the pains do not subside, then heat this cautery which is called "points", as follows:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After applying the cautery to all around the patient's ear, or in and around both of them where the pain is present on both sides, then move away a little from the root of the ear after you have indicated its location. Apply ten points around each ear; treat the area until it has healed completely.
de la torture de la bouche	From the pain in the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Pain that needs to be treated with a cautery is not for those that move from pus, as we have said in the divisions of diseases; and no cautery should be done on symptoms that come from drying skin and scabs.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this instance of pain that moves from pus in the ear and from discharges from the head and gargling, if it responds well, then you must apply a cautery to the hair with three applications: one on the root of the ear, and another slightly beyond the temple, and the third at the adjustment of the two lips; place the cautery where health opens, and make it cauterize that area above the ear up a bit under the eardrum, and another one on the temple as long as an inch; let the cautery stay there until half the wick is burned; this is how you should perform the cautering:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you see the appearance of the surgical instrument that we described earlier, but it is somewhat more delicate, so it should be advisable to have the knives a little bit larger. After treating the wound as I said before, until it has healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When dealing with apoplexy that's been present for a long time and you're treating it as we've said, and if the patient doesn't improve, and the patients don't have fever, then do this: make three applications of the cautery: two on the two horns above the head, one behind the head, and one where the neck is called "vassel" as we previously mentioned, and the last application on the mouth of the stomach; and treat it as we said before.
de litargie	from liturgy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this illness, give the patient large bread and pills that soothe the brain; after that, have all of their head shaved, and then place the sinapic plaster on the back of the head as written or described in the treatment guide for plasters; and here is how to do the cautery: do it in the way I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it's healed like this, well and good; if not, then perform three cauteries descending from the head to the neck. Leave a space of one and a half inches between each cauterization mark. Proceed with treatment as usual. If you see an adjustment needed, and the patient tolerates it, do another cauterization in the middle area; and if necessary, apply two others over the first two marks until it is healed. And use those cauteries that are called 'olive-shaped', just like I've previously mentioned.
de la froidor dou chief	from coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary to cleanse the head of old dandruff and what we have mentioned before; after washing the head with water, then apply heat to it. Perform cauterization around the head and on each horn, one behind and three on the spine near the neck; and if you need more, when the horns are wet and the skin is sore, and the illness is severe, do four cauterizations on the spine at the back; and leave until the driest part of your burn is done, then lift your hand. Afterwards, treat it until it heals properly, and use those cauteries that are called 'olive-shaped', as we have mentioned before.
de l’epilempsie	From epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptics should only use a cautery for those who are phlegmatic, and first modify the brain with years and other remedies that we have mentioned in the section when the patient is large and suffering from physical medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it's an infant who cannot endure this treatment, make them gargle and chew often with good meats; after that he restores his head in the middle, and I do a single cautery according to what we have said previously, and a single cautery on the jugular vein, and on each horn; and if the patient is large and suffering, perform the cauterizations as I told you when dealing with paralysis and softening of body parts, on the spinal column and the neck, and do the olive oil cauterizations according to the method that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is an infant, then you should perform one subtle cautery in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to the cause of melancholy are excesses or fluids corrupted and full of pus, then the part cautery of the fire cautery as we have said to those who have paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to the cause of melancholy is the excess descending into melancholy, and the parts are moist with malaise, then this should be drunk so that the brain may be purified, as was discussed in the previous section.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After touching the part of malaise; after make two linen strips well done, as one circle, place them around the head; and if malaise is felt, you will cross them, held tightly from all sides; then present the liniment, and apply butter of old beeswax; and heat it on a moderate fire, so that it can be applied without causing discomfort; after this, empty the ring inside with the head in place, and let it cool down; and do this once every week to each malaise part with another good administration until they are cured.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere. Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	If you see that the fire cautery is being used, by making several points all over it at once. This way of applying the cautery moistens the brain greatly; and then place wet cotton in butter and in gelatine grease.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the onset comes to the eyes first through the symptoms I have mentioned in the division, then start and continue making the patient drink things that purify the head, and keep him/her away from all moisture, and make them sweat or take baths several times on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After giving him/her instructions about his/her head, and make them undergo cautery on the head, and make two cauterizations on each temple when their eye pressure begins to be felt together in both eyes, or if it is only one eye, then apply all the cautering across all the veins and arteries that are around the brain, and keep them cauterized as long as you can according to the width of the temples; and watch for bleeding, and if you see too much blood coming out, stop the bleeding with such force as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	And I will teach you about the extraction of arteries and incisions with the cautery, how to apply it; and never should you do cautering or remove an arrow from between the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	of the tears' two courses
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	When the tears from the eyes are old and accustomed, and located on the veins, or beneath the arteries that appear outside of the head; and one sees that they are cold excesses of phlegm. So I make him apply the cautery that I have said at the beginning regarding descending to the eyes: 1. Apply it around the head, and 2. two cauteries on each temple, and 3. two cauteries where removing an arrow would be done beneath the two bones; and if there is need for more, carefully apply the cautery above the eyebrows with every small application of the cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	of the tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you administer the remedies according to what we have said in the division, and if they do not benefit, then give the patient three raw onions to drink; after that, place him on his head, and apply a cautery or olive oil in the middle of it; and perform two cauteries with the "claw" type cautery on the two ears, slightly above the hairline; and be careful not to touch the artery, so as not to interfere with it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery which is called "claw".
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare». de coi ci est li forme:	When the paper of the oil is softened due to illness and moisture, then apply this type of cautery which is called "olive". And here is its form:
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see that two cauteries should be made on the two hairs as long as they are; and do not let your hand rest until a third part of the paper is burned away, according to the manner I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	The hair which pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	No instance has occurred where the hair of the eye turns inside out and pricks the eye; in such cases, one performs cauteries according to two methods: that is to say by fire or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so that they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they grow and are even, then make the patient healthy; afterwards draw on the page of the eyes a figure that is as round as the leaf of a laurel tree, and start drawing from the sign at the beginning of the hair. Then place wet cotton in egg white paste and garlic paste on the eye, then heat up the cautery which has this shape:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing on the figure you have drawn a little bit each time, until the scabs cover the area; and the signs of health are that you see the page white, and the hairs lifted at the edge of the eye; then lift your hand, and leave it like this for three days, then place wet cotton in butter until the scab is removed; after that apply ointment until it heals completely.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if hairs and the page become soft after this, then reapply the cautery on that same area as you did initially; and if the hairs have fallen out, then cauterize until the page is lifted to its natural position, and even, and doesn't touch the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The burning medical cautery commands the patient to let the hairs grow large and even; then take parchment to form it like a bay leaf. Then take French soap and live vinegar, each about half an ounce, and finely grind them together. Mix them quickly so they don't cool down. Spread this on the form resembling a bay leaf on paper, and place it under the eyes; if the illness lasts for only one day, you must cut open in one place, and if in both places equally. Place moistened cotton below each eye like an egg. The patient's head should be clean and you should hold your finger in the medicine every time the patient feels the irritation of the medicine, because it feels irritation as well as from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When this has been done for some time, once you have exposed the medicine to your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien. Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the irritation has passed, lift your finger from the medicine, and check if you see the paper lifted as it would be after being forced off by fire or through incision; and if that is the case, then everything is well. If not, apply more medicine to your finger until the medicine works equally on both sides, and the eyes are properly aligned; then place moistened cotton in butter until the burned skin is covered, after that cure the application of the ointment called 'dyafenis' and other remedies, until it heals completely.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.  Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if this requires that you prepare well for your work by great care so that no medicine is wasted on them. And if the paper becomes damp afterwards, and the hair touches in the eye, then repeat the medicine on that part of the eye which was softened with clean paper properly; just as you did before; after this treatment until it is healed; and this is the form of the leaf of wormwood:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of humans vary in size and proportion, and according to this guide your measurements; do not let the right path be denied to him who is studying this craft.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	regarding the treatment of fistula with a cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your treatments are not beneficial, then it is necessary for you to apply cautery according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place their head in your healthy hand; and guide the doctors' head between your hands in such a manner that it does not move or depart from its place; afterwards, stuff cotton moistened with the yolk of an egg or garlic juice onto the eye; next, heat up the cautery which is part of this method: and place it over the head as if forming a peacock's feather; if you see it, may it be pointed between one ear and another, and if you see it, may it also resemble a tent; but in all cases, what is beside that should not move for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula if it has been opened, and treat the putrefaction, and dry it; and if it is closed, open it again, and remove from the wound. Afterwards, apply heat over the cautery in this form, and hold your hand on the cautery at the part below the nose above the eye, so that your hand does not cause mischief; and place the cautery into the oil grease, and let it become contaminated.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien. Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse .iij. jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se .xl. jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, that would be well. If not, then continue with another round of cautery and do this if needed as many times as necessary, leaving it for three days; after that place cotton saturated in butter on it, and use the desiccant ointment dressing while the wound is still clean. Once forty days have passed without healing, apply a corrosive water medicine until the bone is uncovered; and follow the instructions according to what he prescribes in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent. Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure .i. camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	And there is a way to cauterize a fistula that none of the old ones mentioned. Understand what I mean by a fistula, and make it round in shape; after this, place one thin camel bone inside the opening.
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And I do it to the size of about three inches in length; and hold your hand or camel firm, not allowing the muscles to move, so that the melted wax doesn't drip into his eye; and when one places on the eye a wet cotton in the shape of an eggshell or in ashes: the wax performs the work of the hole and brings marvelous healing.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin. Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	And if the fistula is healed through the cautery method we've described, that's good. If not, then it is necessary to use wormwood for the child, and bring the fistula back into the body according to what should be done in its own proper place.
des crevaices en levres	of mouth ulcers
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Occasionally, mouth sores appear on the lips which are called "whiskers", and similarly on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these mouth sores with the methods we've discussed in divisions, and if treatment doesn't help, then use a small surgical tool like this to gently burn them:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it quickly into those cuts until they grow just enough; afterwards, clean the wound of wax while it is still healthy.
de l’aposteme de la goule	from the phlegm in the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When abscesses come to the root of the throat or in the lymph node, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, it leads to putrefaction and decay; after which it hardens and turns into a fistula. You treat this as we have instructed in divisions, but if it doesn't improve, then you need .i (one) cautery according to the size of the fistula; after removing the pus or pustule from the fistula, hold your hand until the metal rod reaches the bottom and up to the root. Then do this once or twice, after the treatment we have mentioned in cures, while it's still healthy. And if treated like this is good; but if not, you need to expose the wound and remove the rotten bone as you find it in your manual.
dou movement des dens	movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines but this doesn't work, then put the head of the disease in your health; afterwards heat up the cautery until its form comes after in such a way that you place a twig on the tooth. And put within the cautery a hot stick, and keep your hand steady so that the diseased part feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; after lift your hand and start using the cautery according to your desire; afterwards fill the diseased part's mouth with salt water, and leave it for an hour and then pull it out.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this manner the moving tooth is repositioned, and the softened gum becomes restrained, and the moisture that was present dries up.
de la dolor des dens	from the pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When tooth pain comes from coldness, or there is cold or heat inside the body, and medical treatments do not help, then one must use cautery according to two methods: and butter cautery and fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Butter cautery works like this: you take butter from a cow, and in a spoon made of iron or tin; afterwards take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a thread, then soak it in melted butter, and place it on the painful tooth quickly and hold until it cools down; and do this several times until its effectiveness reaches to the root of the tooth, and if you see wet wool and cotton soaked in cold butter, place them again on the aching tooth, and apply hot iron for as long as heat reaches inside the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain. Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	Fire cautery works like this: you take a hot iron or tin rod, so large that the fire does not reach inside the wound; after heating the cautery, from which the heat will come out afterwards, place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the heat of the cautery cools down; do this repeatedly, as the pain will be gone that day or the next. And ensure that the patient fills their mouth with plenty of butter while the process is happening, then pull it out quickly; this is how to use a fire cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And apply the cautery to whatever part you desire, according to your capacity; and this is how it forms the rod:
des scrophules	of the sores
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait ij. aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou .ij. se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi .iij. jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the sores are due to cold blood and moisture, and do not respond to digestion by medicines, then apply the cautery as described below, and make two openings for the vapors to escape from the other side; and place the heated cautery on the abscess once, or twice if needed, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, adjust the cautery according to the size of the abscess, and leave it in that position for three days; and apply moistened cotton with butter until the scabs are removed; afterwards cure with ointments and bandages until it heals.
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc. Aprés li fai .i. autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the moisture invades through the channels of the lungs and especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the body be cleansed first with diuretic medicines; afterwards apply the cautery at the root of the throat, and make sure not to go all the way to the throat but just a little bit. Afterward do another application of cautery at the junction between the neck and the base of the spine, and it is from this type of cautery that we have our form depicted ahead; and treat after as described until it heals completely.
de la toust	In respect to cautery by fire, it commands the diseased person to allow hair growth until it becomes long and uniform; and if they prick at their origin, it holds the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et .i. autre cautere emmi le pis entre .ij. mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and the diseases of the stomach are due to cold moisture, and patients do not have fever nor dryness, and it's an old disease, then make the burnings on their strength in their veins; and one other burning under their buttocks between the two nipples; and let the burning called 'claw-like' be according to the form that was mentioned before.

de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	From the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement. dou cautere de pleuresin	apply the weeping cautery

The old ones said that one should do pleuresin cauterizations using the roots of aristological plants, and here's how to do it: take a long root of aristological plant, the longest you can find, ensure it's dry, and make sure it's as thick and as long as your thumbs; then mix it with oil, heat it on fire, and apply one cautery between the jawbone and neck, and two small ones slightly below where the beard is; also apply four cauterizations between the fifth and sixth ribs, leaning a bit behind; apply one in the armpit and another on the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and make sure your hand doesn't press too much but rather does it smoothly as if smelling.

de ydropisie	Of cautery by fire, command the ill patient to allow hair growth until long and even; and if they pierce at their root, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.

Cautery is not suitable for ydropique, except through the method called "asclytes". Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After allowing the cauterization to set for a long time due to putrefaction, and do not cease the treatment of the disease after the cauterization; and recovery would hasten, and both the four intentions with God's help would be together.

de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	Regarding the inflammation known as 'thelul'

de plaie mal curee	from poorly treated wounds
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient's body cannot endure cutting or incision, as we will describe in its place, if there arises a disease that cannot be cured except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When there is no issue of pus and it's old and corrupted due to putrefaction and moisture, if you need to determine its extent entirely with one test, make sure that you know how far this test has penetrated. After heating the cautery until it resembles a sharp tool, place the tip into the fistula according to the amount that the test has entered, and continue using the cautery until all putrid and corrupted pus is burned away, once or twice or thrice depending on your need; be careful not to burn nerves or major veins. If the fistula goes through the body of the bladder and intestines, take these precautions, and do this only in the intestinal area, remembering that it isn't complete until finished. After treating the area until it is healed, when pus has been removed and materials have hardened over time, then you can determine if it is fully healed. If the materials have not hardened, know that there is still pus present within, and the bone has become corrupted at its base; and thus as one of these we shall speak about in his area.
de la maladie des reins	Regarding kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When the abdominal pain originates from the kidneys and due to large wind, it affects women more so than men, then you must perform a cautery on both sides of the kidneys with an iron rod as we have previously described; and if we apply the cautery centrally, there will be three lines of cauterization, which will provide greater relief.
de la vessie	From the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is thick and weak from heat and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then apply a cautery to the lower part of the bladder, where the pubic hair begins, and one on each side, and let each cautery be as long as your fist; and do one behind the back, or two if you need them; and make the cauteries in a cross shape according to the form described before.
de la marris	Of the mare's urine
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the mare's heat is cold and moist, and fails to allow conception, and her flowers are rotten with delayed termination; and when they come, she feels great pain: then it should be that you apply three cauterizations inside the womb, as we have said or like the bladder cautery, and two cauterizations behind the back; and make the cauterizations in a cross shape, as we have said.
de la hainche	From the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous mucus descends into the hip socket, and due to this reason it moves out of its place. The signs are that one leg is longer than the other when measured together; and when you find the knee at the point where you would see it normally, you should cauterize the hip socket with a fire cautery similar to half-circle shape. And mark in front of the thigh as she turns, so that the socket is inside the circle. And let the cautery be like those used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the fire cautery is not at your disposal, make three large olive-shaped cauteries, and let these cauteries also be perfectly round like all the knuckles. And treat it while it remains sound.
de la dolor de la hainche	The pain in the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the thigh bone area, and this is due to coldness and moisture, and the treatment is as we have discussed for division and cure failures, and the illness is old: then you must cleanse the patient of large thick body fluids with pus-filled pills or other good-looking pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see that the circle cauterization as we've mentioned before in relation to hip joint dislocations; but do it this way so that all the hips are contained within the circles, and all parts of the bone burn.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.
