And this is the way to treat sciatica, when pain remains in the hip and does not reach up to the thigh nor down to the leg. And if it reaches as far as the thigh and leg, then two cauterizations should be done where the patient says the pain stays, and one above the ankle on the fourth day, at the left side a little bit; and make sure these are cutaneous cauterizations, burn off any thick spots along veins; and if the patient feels that the pain extends as far down to the knee or close to it, then cauterize where he feels the pain, three points or four on the cauterized area which is called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if more work is needed, then do it; and if the pain extends from the knee towards the thigh, use a cutaneous or circular cautery on that area, and make sure you take good care in all your cauterizations so as not to leave them incomplete such that you burn nerves and major arteries, and do not cause the patient any greater discomfort or constriction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I have seen several instances where cauterization was done on the ankle up to the knee, and they left it until the leg swelled completely, and the feet as well, causing them to be pierced and corrupted throughout. After a stomach treatment from which she died.

Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This disease often affects young children, and the signs of its beginning are that they become pale when they stand alone, and faint; and you find a swelling in the last spine of the back and an appearance that comes over other spines.

If you see this and observe it being treated, apply the hot iron to each part of the spine equally. Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain is caused by moisture spread throughout each limb, and when pain comes from the foot, which they call "gout" properly, and when it's due to cold reasons and its cures are made with medicines that can't heal it, then it should be treated using cauterization in this manner: make a hole inside the joint of the foot, and have olive oil cauterizations according to this shape:

de la routure dou syfac	Of the rupture in the uterus
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When dislocation occurs in the shoulder, and the muscles descend to the chest this is newly happening, it's necessary that when you see them being treated, do not disturb him during the day; and use things that relax his stomach, so that the intestines descend from his belly; after make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to shave his underbelly until the muscles are repaired, then bring him back to your fingers, and mark along the rupture above the bone of the elbow, and ensure every sign is like half a circle above the torso; then heat up the cautery which is formed thus:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	As long as it's white and smells of farts. Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. de dolor anciene en aucun membre	from old pain in no limb

de meselerie	In mixture
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The remedies are applied once by cautery with great assistance, and equally the illness that comes from the putrefaction of bile and melancholy. Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the mixture is everywhere scattered; and it becomes apparent, then it is necessary that you cauterize with these cauteries we have said on the head, and one cauterization under the nose, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the buttocks and another elsewhere, and two on each shoulder; and two on the ribs, and two on the tendons of the foot, and one on each joint of hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and guard against the nerves that are at the heel, do not burn them; and never do any cauterization on the bone under the fingernails, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that when I make more cauteries, I provide more help, and he benefits from them; and know that the patient does not feel pain during cautery as a healthy person would, because his body is already completely corrupted. And it is necessary for the cautery to be large and small according to the limbs and joints, in accordance with what you will find in manuals on metalwork. After treatment, rub the area several times with honey and other remedies until it becomes clean.
de enfleure	of inflamed
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When inflammation appears in any limb and is treated with medicines, oils, and bandages, but remains unwell, then I make cauteries on the limb according to the size of the limb; and let each cautery go somewhat into the heart of the lesion; then treat it with poultices until it becomes well. And for each time a cautery is made, do so at the hand, foot and back, at the exit of the nerve that paralyzes the limb, and in this way the inflammation is removed; and still no one should interfere unless they are knowledgeable about limbs and the exits of moving nerves within the body.
de albaras	From woad
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the sickness which is called "albaras" grows old, and the field of medicine cannot help it, then cauterize slightly with a cautery according to the quantity of the fur in the keur, until the bladder is removed and its color changes; then wash with flour several times and lentils using rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood from colon and water from an almond tree, each part from one. Mix all together, wrap it with a cloth, and keep under the sun until healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment for the sore by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When the sore begins, and you see it stop, then apply the cautery using a circle-shaped tool that seems appropriate. And always let those who advise you know to also cauterize in the center of the sore; and I do not think this is good because I fear it might lead to erosion and corruption and I have already had no intention to do so at any time; and more sensible practice would be to cauterize around, with the tool that's called "circul", as we explained about types of cautery.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	Of the swelling that cannot perish
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it is lingering to die or due to the excess it produces or because of the old age in which illness occurs (that is, when one is too old) and there is little blood, or due to strength; then you see its hastening towards death: therefore cauterize internally with a few small cauterizations. Afterwards leave it like that. For it will hasten towards dying.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see her pierced through with the entire cautery, then heat up the cautery in accordance to what is described:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And place your hand in the middle of this disease called "adubelati" as long as the cauteries have pierced through its core, and make sure that these cauteries are such that the illness feels it being pushed out to such an extent that the process of putrefaction is accelerated. After treating until it has been completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The treatment with a fire cautery using a iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another method of disease called "corrodens", which is nothing else but a gangrene of the limb because it sears the limbs like iron sears dry wood. If you see this disease that can be treated with combined fire cautery, then apply small and large iron cauterizations according to what is suitable for the location or where the disease is present; after applying the cautery from all sides until you remove all corruption, leave nothing behind so that everything corrupted is removed. Then let it rest for three days, and apply suffering with oil on the cauterized areas until the burnt skin and all corruption are gone. After this ointment cure of pus. And if you see after three days that no healthy flesh has grown, it's good; but if this doesn't happen, reapply the cautery to what is still corrupted in the limbs. This disease can sometimes be cured with an ague medicine instead of a fire cautery treatment; however, fire cautery is much more helpful and I have already spoken about the cure for ague disease in its specific section: take it as needed when you require it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of hernias that come to stones
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Sometimes there is a disease born outside the body that we call "clos," according to our understanding, and it's a large protruding thing that hurts the foot. And for this illness of clos, there are two ways of applying cauterization. That means, you need to heat one cautery like a feather from a goose, and make it out of good iron at the size which can hold a nail in every direction, with thin edges; after this, put everything hot on the nail, and move your hand right around the nail until it reaches the tip of the nail; then leave it thus for three days until pus begins to form; afterwards apply an ointment made from ground wild marjoram mixed with oil, and let the ointment stay overnight, and the nail will fall out from its roots. Then treat the area with salve until the wound heals completely.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if it is converted from the outside on the body, and this happens repeatedly both in hands and feet, then you should apply hot water cautery; and here's how to do it: take a spider's hair or iron rod, or a goose feather, place them above the nail and the althelul (meaning blisters or warts), and put the rod such that it touches all around. Then pour some hot water onto it, hold your hand tightly in position, squeeze while moving your hand until the edge of the rod reaches the root of the nail, then you will find the hot water penetrates deeply down to the root; let the patient tolerate this for a bit, and they will be free from the irritation of the hot water for an hour. Then leave it thus, and everything at its roots will come out completely. Do this another time until you have removed all those on the body, then treat with salves that generate flesh.
li cure dou trembler	he treats through trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some shake due to cold or nerves or a quartan fever or other affliction, it is necessary that you perform four or five cauteries on the spine of their back. One cautery between each vertebra; one on the chest at the olive cautery; if this doesn't stop shaking, and quickens the recovery from the cold ailment.
des pustules puans	pus-sores
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	When visible through openings in the body's surface, or pus-sores that originate from thick putrid matter, they are a result of this process. Upon their first appearance, it is necessary at once when they appear to cauterize each head of the pustule: a subtle firewood stick cautery, where the tip touches the flame, or a long root of the aristologue herb, or a lenticular (round) cautery. And one should not cauterize them at their start when they first appear, following this method; instead, it discharges all excess that has come from them and leaves them healed. But it is required that this be done after the blood's evacuation.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery has been cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times great hemorrhages occur from the artery that has been cut at the wound coming to the outside, or during incising of an abscess, or due to the cautery on a limb, and similar things; it is very distressing when the smell becomes unbearable.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And still, when this happens to no one, if you hasten to place your index finger on the wound of the vein and press it very much until the skin is relieved under your finger, and no drop comes out; then light several small and large olive oil cauteries until they are all red. Then take .i., or large or small according to the wound and limb where the artery is located, and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and keep the cautery there until the skin is completely cooled.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cauteries are off the fire, then take hastily another one of the cauteries that are on the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing this one after the other until the bone is completely healed; and watch that you do not burn the nerve which lies beneath, and that no harm comes to the patient; and know that when a bone dislocates from an artery, one cannot properly heal it themselves when the artery is large, unless done through one of the four ways we have mentioned: by cautery, by extraction if it has not been treated, by strong thread binding or by medicine applied which has the power to heal blood; and then bind and keep it steady for the future.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will administer the reattachment by tightly binding with cloths or by placing burning things on, or other similar actions, if it does not help then it likely won't.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and they have no tool or medicine at hand, then they should place their thumb on the wound of the vein as we said, and stretch it well until it is healed above the wound and above the vein; and do not move their finger, but often moisten it with cold water so that it stays very cold until the bone is frozen, swollen and healed. And prepare for cautery and medicines what needs to be done.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book of treatments for amputations
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have spoken about the first chapter on all diseases where it is necessary to apply a heat cautery, or hot medicine, and their causes, instruments, and forms; and we placed that chapter up until the knee, and I will continue this chapter in the same manner so as to find what seems easier for whoever wishes to know.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And as I begin this one, it is necessary that you understand that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first section about cauteries, which means greater caution must be exercised.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I advise you not to undertake foolishness. For many ways of people come into cures. Some come from those who become quite afflicted with their illness that they die lightly due to the despair they find in their disease, and the severity of their wickedness; and one must have fear towards these things.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And of these there are who give their understanding, and say: "Wait, I am good." And the illness is spiteful. It is not fitting that you agree with those who come to you in this manner, but rather place more stringent consideration for your honor than for your greed, and do not act foolishly but wisely from what you are certain of and have experienced; and use prediction and indication in treatments for illnesses where health has been transformed; and this will assist you in acquiring good reputation, glory, and long-lasting remembrance.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear child, our lords provide good understanding and righteousness to you, and if you wish to aspire from the holy inspiration of their hand, so be it.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered this chapter out of discussion by chapters, according to what is before or the chapter about the cauteries, which I discussed from the head up until the foot, because you will find it easier that which you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	from the head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease comes very often to children at birth, and when the mother presses too hard on the head of the child; and it happens in no other instance due to a reason that we know.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease in anyone other than children, and among all those I've observed, their death was hastened by it; for this reason, it seems to me that it is worth stopping the treatment with these remedies.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child of this kind where the shoulder was full of water, and the head swelled each day until it couldn't support more weight; and feared so much from the moisture that he died, and this moisture is assembled beneath the bone within the socket, between the muscle and the bone. And the openings are such when the moisture is between the muscle and the bone, and the abscesses are small, that you make a wide cut in the head one groove; and be so long as two fingers, as long as the moisture runs; and here see the shape of the spathile:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If there is more moisture, and the abscesses are larger, make two cuts in a cross-like manner, according to this shape:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and you see the openings of the head's edges from each part, and water leaks when you press it inside with your hand, and this does not stop: then it is necessary that you make three cuts in the middle of the head in this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision, remove all moisture outside. After holding the cuts of cloths and powders, then put wine and oil, and leave like this until the fifth day; then reset it, treat the wound by changes and ointments, and let the head also heal equally. Afterwards, allow the patient to eat dry meat from a bit of moist until the limb is comfortable and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look at where the large opening of the abscess is, and gather water; for it is never in front, nor behind; neither to the right, nor to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut then the place where the abscess opens, and fill with water, and make a cut according to your ability; and be careful not to cut the artery; watch for blood flow, so that the patient dies from blood loss and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	Of cautery from fire, command the sick person to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it comes to any disease which is called "catarrh" in the eyes or at the bottom, and this sickness is old, and the treatment with medicine does not help, then the last resort therapy would be cautery using which one cuts off the two great arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief. de emigrainne	"De emigrainne" translates to "from grain" or possibly referring to a process of sifting or removing grains. Without further context, it's challenging to provide an exact interpretation for this specific phrase within the medieval medical treatise. In general terms, in a medical setting, it could relate to procedures involving the removal of grains (such as pieces of gravel or sand) from bodily tissues or fluids.

de l’estoupement des oreilles	On the cauterization of ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that enters into the ears is one of four things: or grains, or beast, or mine stone or similar thing like iron; or seed, such as beans, peas; or flowing substance like water and sweat and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When what he excretes into the ear is a piece or another way of thing that doesn't fit in the ear, nor grows in the ear, place the ear under the sun. If you see the stone, if any drop of violet oil or nut oil distills out, then proceed with extraction; and have them sneeze pepper, and block the nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put pieces of cloth or wool into the ear; and hold the ear up. Many times this remedy works; and if it does not work in that way, have them extract using fine forceps, as is described here:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out with the forceps, that's good; if not, proceed with extraction using a small delicate instrument of two halves. And if it doesn't jump out by that means, make an arachnid stick and press out its head or part of the stick near the ear strongly, and block the wick in the middle of the candle or rosemary to the extent that nothing can enter through the candlestick with the stick; then pull it forcefully as we have said; and if it does not work in this manner, take some glue from this substance and place a small instrument on it at a suitable point for doing so, and put a bit of cotton inside. Then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull it forcefully.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not heal from all these things that we have said, hurry to cut the ear in this way, allowing pus and blood to flow out, and spasms; and the manner of cutting is such that you first make a sinner on the cephalic side of the patient, and remove some of the blood according to its measure. Then let the patient sit between your hands and turn their ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear in the fatty area hanging down; and let the cut be like a crescent moon until you reach the bone. Then break the bone according to your strength, and suck it quickly into your mouth; and the cure as long as it is sound.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if they are grains and it is inflamed, administer an extraction; and if it cannot come out, administer one of these small incisions according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. de l’estoupement des oreilles	Regarding ear piercing.
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a bit of ear wax; and this same thing happens with injuries or birth in the ear, causing eardrops that only come once inside the ear if they cannot be seen; and never do two drops of ear wax appear at once, you see them well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Thus, the one that comes inside if you cannot see it, is due to a blockage in various positions, and here what needs to be done becomes clear: you should place the ear near the sun; look inside: if you can see the plaque apparent, if the work has fully formed this pus-like substance from which we are speaking:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be so, cutting in front and behind it completely flat, so that it does not irritate the ear; if there is a plaque or bump from inside the ear or of the ear itself, if you have fine pincers, use them to carefully cut, until all the char has been removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the operations have gone too far in the ear, take one thin and light rasor, scrape a small piece from fire, then place it inside the ear. If you feel the operation causing pain to your ears, pierce lightly, and ensure not to injure the nerves of the ear; then insert into the ear a patch according to the width of the tear, and apply the moisture in the Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Continue this for as many days as the wound is healing, or take a patch and moisten it with rose water, then sprinkle powdered vitriol over it. And if you see swelling in the ear, it should be that you remove the patch and apply another wetted patch made from rose oil and beeswax, until the swelling is removed; then treat it until it is well healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, soak a cloth and wet it with cold water, then put it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding which are similar to those used for distillations.
de la char des papieres	From the residue of paper
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	In the process of unfolding hairs when they are moist and drying, it is necessary to use tweezers and forceps on them. Take a small slice from their roots; then place under the glass tube.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if you do not remove the thorns, cauterize them with a thin round cautery iron. After incision, it's worth removing them; and they are often cut again, because nothing remains from their roots. And when they are cauterized by fire, those root parts burn and never return.
de la gresle	Regarding ice
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times, in the papers come things that seem greasy by their form and hardness, and because of this it is called "grains", which is an assembly of moisture thick on the paper above and below; the operations are like this: take care if the grains move from one side to another, and this is a simple thing to know; then do it broadly, then lightly cauterize each part, then hold them with tweezers, and cut. If you cannot cut without piercing a bit of the paper, or causing harm to the patient; and if the tear is large, and there's an assembly at one seam, treat until it heals; and if it's small, do not use force, for the ointments will heal it quickly and regenerate tissue.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the grains descend into the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper, and place the grains on tweezers, cut and press from both sides; and if the paper is moved away by the incision, it causes no harm; and when the grains are cut, remove the salty water, treat the surrounding area until the tissues regenerate; as long as the patient heals.
de la graisse des eulz	of the grease of the lumps
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a fat that accumulates on the surfaces of paper sheets, and this happens more often in children than in adults, causing great pain to their eyes, and they experience an excess of tears in the mornings; thus, they cannot look at the sunlight as tears tend to flow into their eyes; for this reason, they lie down next to their beds, sleep on them, and have their paper sheets moist under their eyes. And when you press your hand onto it with your fingers, you can feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the way to treat it is such that you have your patient's head in a healthy position. Then take one piece of linen cloth and set up as tent-like structure into a circular shape according to the amount of exinach present in each section, then place it on top; press with your hands from both sides so that all the exinach is gathered within the circle. Afterward, cut in the middle of the moisture, making a small slit not larger than the wound made when opening veins, and ensure that the linen reaches into the moisture completely. Then various sections of the exinach come out through this slit, resembling the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Pull out then, in one piece, the cloth padding between your fingers on the outside, and twist your hand to the right and left until it is spread; make sure not to block the slit, that you reach all the way into the moisture up to the eyes, do not hurt.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the exit does not open at the start of the incision, increase a bit the incision gently until it opens; then treat it as we have said, then moisten with bandages and water, place it on the wound, and apply binders.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are those who grind grain and place it to corrupt the moisture that has remained. Then treat until they become clean. And when an abscess forms at the wound, then apply plaster remedies until they become clean.
des poilz des papieres	(of paper hairs)
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hair grows in other than its natural place and ages, it harms the eyes, causing various diseases like familiar infections and paper weakening or scarring, as well as white discharges due to this cause; and one treats accordingly with four methods: either by combined fire cautery, or through ague medicine as described previously in the section on cautery, and is done through cutting and sewing, or through sutures, according to what I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you place the tip of the eyelid in your healthy state, then turn the paper of the eye with your left hand; if it flips properly, it's good; if not, sew one thread above through at all .i. and attach another thread over the entire sheet of paper, and then turn it with a sharp tool; then cut in the area under the paper, under the displaced hairs, from the major tear to the minor tear; then remove the thread, place a small cotton tent on top of the paper along with a piece of silk, and then sew an outline resembling a leaf, like the bay leaf, onto the paper. Yet it is necessary that the shape match the amount you see when lifting the lifted paper.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if it is necessary to cope with a large quantity of paper according to how the paper has become soft; then do this for all parts around the tear lines that you have indicated, starting from the major tear and going until the minor. And make sure one of the tears is close to the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then place the needle into one of the two corners of the tear, then scrape off everything; then join both lips with a stitch using a needle and all .i. fine thread, and let out any blood, and air the excess threads on the two tear lines, if you are able to do this; but if not, don't worry about it, and leave the stitches open for .iij. or .iiij. days; then heal the wound without a stitch with dry and binding substances, as the paper heals in response to the healing of the wound and its joining together, but the stitch becomes loose (as the old ones would say), which is work without fear.
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if you choose another way: and it is that you mark the paper with a shape as round as the leaf of myrtle, just like we've recounted, in three inches cut according to this form:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut the one that sits above evenly, according to this form:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you do not have the ability to hold the forceps, and if the thing is not equal, take one thread or needle with two threads; and place that thread inside the figure. And place another thread under the large suture line, and the second thread under the small one, and assemble the threads equally between your fingers. Then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin over which you have marked, just as we recounted, then sew both edges of the wound by stitching, and treat until it is healed; and if pus comes to your incision, soothe it with ointments and similar healing substances;
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And it is sometimes the case that the hair on paper changes: if it is necessary for you to use what we have said about incisions; but the stitches in one and the other are more unnatural.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of canes follows this form: and you should convert the paper and cut it inside according to what I have said, and then make two canes by art, and also two fine threads each as long as the paper and as wide as its thickness; and pinch these two pieces together at half way from the paper of the eye, and hold tight the two canes from their ends shaped respectively; and leave them like this for a few days, and the skin that is constricted will soften and heal and recover, until it discharges through itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If the process takes longer and forces are applied, treat until it is healed; and when the wound has closed and the paper has lifted, and no more hair will grow; this is the form of the two canes that you make according to this figure, and according to this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The tasks are such that you take a delicate needle and tie two pieces of silk thread that are both fine together, then join the heads of each and tie them intricately, making sure the length of the threads is as long as your palm; then prepare another piece of very thin silk thread for sewing, and tie it to your head. Next place the patient's head in a healthy position; ensure sunlight illuminates the operation area because this method requires subtlety and precision. Then insert the needle into the root of the hair where it is adjusted naturally until piercing through paper rapidly as you move it over the natural hair; then pull out all hairs up to the sewing line, tying that hair back into the line if there are two or three or more; finally remove your hand so that all the hairs emerge from the sewing area along with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the operation on the area is complete and hair doesn't come out with it, then pull the line away from the other end of the thread you have prepared until you see your hand through the vision of the eye; then pull the line and the thread, and keep the eye closed for two or three days, as long as the hair hardens in its place and grows flesh at the spot; and if the hairs are small, accompany them with one long natural hair, hold it up like you would this, until it is straightened out then raise it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Regarding eye infections or diseases.
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease, called 'aleacrati' or gangrene comes to the eye, there are two ways: one natural and another unnatural. It occurs suddenly from wounds, or from surgery or cautery, and by similar actions.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the method of this surgery for it is that you split that seam and expose the eyelid, and place linen tents inside, and bind it until it heals; and it should not be that you use in the treatment of it things that dry up and restrict. For if you do this, then the disease will return worse than the first one; but work with soothing things instead, such as fenugreek; and pour water or boiled water and linen seed into it, and apply the yolks of duck eggs to all oils, and cover it with a tent, and treat it accordingly.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your treatment are that you must be cautious not to join it back together in the same shape as before; and these operations we have described are only remedies for this disease, so that it does not return in the same form as before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the fat which comes to the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease which is about to be truly called "axacrati", and it's natural and accidental. The accidents come from wounds, cuts, cauterizations, and similar things; and the way of this operation in such cases involves you piercing with a needle, having two threads within it, inserting this into flesh, and causing the thread to appear on both sides of the left tear duct as much as possible so that the threads move through the two parts of the flesh. Then the flesh is above the entire needle, and the cloth has two large buttons at its end.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the appearance of the paper follows as it should according to what is required, that's fine; but if not, take a pair and place it in the cut, and turn the paper, creating two cuts where they were inside the paper. Then make the edges of the two cuts from each corner of your incision, so when they are assembled together, the appearance matches that of a letter which has four dots 'i'. Then remove this flesh according to how its borders match up with those of the paper, then reattach the two separated parts with thread made from wool. After this, heal it using treatments as we have spoken about for softening medicines and antiseptics until it's healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness comes from a cut or stitch or cautery, it is necessary that you make a full gash across the hairs of the paper, and follow as before; then cut between the two leaves of one page like I said; and must perform the operation according to the shape of the illness, for she varies greatly in form, and the surgeons arrange their tools in accordance with all their ability so that they can return the figure to its natural form; and even the patients themselves, following the operations and instruments needed from various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	suddenly of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this seam happens in a way that the paper above is fastened with the white of the egg and cannot move or do its natural works, then it must be that you pierce the edge of a razor under the paper, and lift it up; and stretch it out on pins until you reach the fine spatula where it is not too sharp nor too deep, so as to prevent the spatula being too sharp causing pain in the eye; perform your incision, gently removing that which has been assembled together, in such a way that the paper regains its natural form and heals completely. Do not let anything acidic fall into the eye, and rinse it with fresh water and cologne; then place between the paper and the eye a linen tent, and cover the eye with wet wool from an egg; afterwards apply for three days a cool cloth and soothing things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	At the eye's nail
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail of the eye is in two ways: it is nerve-like and resembles a single hard substance, and another which is not nerve-like but seems like frozen moist congeal. If one touches it with iron or cares for it with pins, it cannot; both appearances start from near the large lacrimal gland, grow slowly and gradually until they cover all of the vision, light and movement of the eye.

They are born or emerge from various joints of the body, some resembling scorpions at the end of feet; and if there is a joint with skin colored in red tone, and if it has a yellow skin. In this case, among these joints that are yellow and not enhanced, you should have the patient lie between your hands facing the sun; work their nostrils, and pour wine on those joints, then remove them; then collect what you can hold of the fine sharp tip on one side until you know that this joint is completely ossified.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there is no part that can be handled, when opening the entire body with all its instruments subtilely and lightly, ensuring nothing remains; and if there's not sufficient elevation or abscess encumbrance, then surgically intervene as it should be done; and if it's malignant abscesses, act promptly and use the cautery until the pus is expelled and all the contents are out, then cleanse thoroughly either with water or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	And if it is the nose that's affected and moisture invades up to the palate, know that there is pus present; and if moisture doesn't pass as intended, know that there is newly formed flesh above the bone, so the instruments don't come through properly for cutting: thus, you must introduce a thread of linen somewhat thick, hold it with both hands, and have an inch or less between each knot; and guide the patient's tongue along this thread until the pus comes out from the nose into their mouth; and often children do this at school, and it is a simple task for those who can do it. Hold one head that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and wait to check between each action as we are instructed with the thread present. Do this until you know that the knots have corrupted that flesh, then remove the threads, clean off any blood, oil the thread in Egyptian ointment, and place it back into the nose as before; do this for three days or longer, until the ointments dissolve all that is left of the pus; and then leave a strip of opium paste inside for several more days to heal, and if it requires dry medicine, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purify the head, with which one distills oils and medicines or wine.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And use silver or lead, resembling an open lamp, like a rod, and guide it in the same way; and if you can see it, make a closed rod, and ensure the instruments are filled for purging the head; and have two handles on the head to hold it when heating oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	Of the flesh around the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease is born in the head near the nose, which is called "telul", it grows and becomes large until something visible; hence it must be cut at the beginning, then remove all the bone, then place the cautery or burning medicine on it. And if one delays cutting until it's large, should be careful if it feels hard, changes color, or lacks sensation: don't touch it with iron because it is encrusted pus, for when you cut once, it causes great harm to the patient; and if the pus is due to hot touch not from change in color, and if you see that it can all be cut, drain the patient and let it be operated on fearlessly, and treat its surroundings with dry and restraining substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nose has been cut and sewn together
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when a continuation of the work comes into one of these open joints, it benefits little for some individuals. Therefore, this should not happen to any person, if they examine whether their wound is fresh throughout their blood; and then align the two lips onto a suture, and treat them while they are still healthy; and if the lips have turned black on both sides, you must sear all parts of their skin until they heal, then join the two lips onto a suture, and keep them together, and apply powdered dragon's blood and incense. And put powders one upon another with a plaster piece of strong or any other soldering plaster, and leave it until it discharges by itself, then treat with ointment while they are still healthy.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of suture is that you join the wound: either with needles, as we have said in the abdominal stitch; or with thread, as I've instructed.
des apostemes des levres	from abscesses of lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Hands go inside the wound cavity of an abscess many times, resembling grains sometimes, small and large; therefore you must return to the lips, cut into each one individually, take it with tweezers, remove it from every part; then apply the hand after the vitriol incision, until the pus is drained out; and afterwards wash the hand thoroughly, cleanse the wound of dry matter until it heals.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a piece of attached gum tissue comes out on the gums, which the old would call "albulus"; it should be held with forceps, cut at its root, and leave the bleeding or blood; then put in under the hand vitriol broiet powder, or other powders that restrict and dry out; and if this flesh returns after incision, and many times happens, when it is cut a second time, and cauterized: if it does not return even after the cauterization; and these are the forms for removing them.
des sordens	Of cauteries made with fire, command the sick person to let their hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.
