Certain times, teeth are gathered together at the front of the mouth, between the gums and the inside of the mouth, where the skin is ugly and rough; and at other times teeth turn black, yellow, or have worms until corruption reaches the gum, causing them to stink. So it is necessary that you place your hand on the sick person, with his head in a holy position, and grasp each tooth or piece of flesh as they appear between your fingers, making sure there's nothing left behind; and then do this for blackness, greenness, jaundice, and other colors until they are removed. If what is taken out at first is sufficient, that is good; if not, start again on the second day and third day until you have everything removed; and know that teeth require various tool shapes to be extracted, according to how their work shows them, because the scraper used for tooth extraction has different forms than the one used between teeth; and these shapes and others should be ready with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary that when you treat the tooth for its pain, you delay extraction as much as possible because it should not be done hurriedly; this is due to the nature of the material so that there would not be an excuse for the scraping.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Therefore when the patient is constrained to draw blood, it is necessary that you know exactly where the tooth lies. Many times during this operation, one might think there's a tooth abscessed, and you should check if it's indeed a tooth abscess before drawing blood; and once done, remove the good tooth; but until the bad tooth is extracted entirely, the pain does not disappear completely as you may lose some due to the operation, which we have already explained to these surgeons. And when you are certain of where the tooth lies, it's necessary that you cauterize inside the tooth up to a depth of i spatumile strongly in order to keep the gum from bleeding everywhere; then move your hand or with your fine tongs directly into the first pocket and gently until extraction is complete; then firmly hold the tongs; and have the shoulder of the patient in their saint between your knees, and hold it well so that it doesn't move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if there is no bleeding, take any of these instruments and gently place them inside each part, and move them as you did at first. And if the teeth have been pierced and are mixed together, it's necessary to fill them with cloths where they were lost; and when extracting them carefully with tongs, ensure not to break them during extraction; and it is important to cut very precisely around the gum to remove the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And ensure you do not break it and leave a part behind, causing the patient more intense pain than before. And be aware that this should not be done as some ignorant surgeons do, who break once without hesitation or consideration for the tooth's integrity, and they do not apply what we have advised; but instead, they bring about another painful condition through their haste and recklessness every time due to the roots remaining in place or because of the tooth broken by them; this is something we often want. And when the teeth are extracted, wash off the socket with wine or water, and if bleeding continues as it often does, fill the cavity with vinegar. If that doesn't suffice, cauterize it instead.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the tools, to which one binds their teeth first, should be with long points and thick handles, such that they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And may have large members that do not bend when being pulled, and be made of well-crafted iron, and have teeth for holding as needed.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root stays during extraction, it is necessary that you place inside your mouth a wet cotton ball soaked in butter. For one or two days, until the gums are softened, then take out the forceps called "algefri", which makes the shoulder appear like a care; and make them inside just like a file, this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if they do not want to come out of all these nails, it is necessary that you reveal the flesh entirely along the root and place the tool called "althalus", which means palanchet, as its form is shown here:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it is free and large enough so that it does not break at all, and if the root jumps out through this, that's good; if not, use all the tools you have available, as their forms are shown here afterwards:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this tool which has two points, as its form is shown here:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and there are other tools placed according to the order of teeth, and this tool that appears to be large tweezers, as its form is shown here:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And be it this instrument that cannot break it, and know that there are few instruments of teeth; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise surgeons themselves find their own instrument by themselves, according to what their operations and diseases indicate him, because there are parts of diseases for which old teachers did not teach an instrument due to the diversity of these ones and so they do not break from a fracture or of the other bones, or if it rots, then he searches among the instruments that he needs, as I have told you, and helps with gestures, from which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be them large and well holding for holding the bone that it does not escape but that you may hold and remove it; then restore its place with medicines fitting to this, and if there is decay in the bone and it is small, seek all this instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to its natural form, and the shape is ugly, especially in virgin girls, you should know if this tooth has been born after another tooth, and it is not straight in place, and one cannot polish or file it: then you must extract it; and if it adheres with a tooth, take this instrument as depicted here, which resembles two small beaks, and it should be made of sharpened iron.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the tooth is inserted gradually into one's hand due to its hardness and because you don't move others, and if it can be seen that we could grind it, then this tooth is ground with a single grinding wheel as it is formed:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And similarly to the file used for making needles; and grind the tooth gradually into one's hand lightly over time, so that it doesn't move until it cuts; then make it flat at the end with all nozzles, and if it is too sharp and it irritates the tongue, then you must grind off the roughness until it is even, so that it doesn't irritate the tongue or spoil speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth becomes loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the tooth is in front of the mouth, or by percussion or by falling, and the patient can't press on what they're chewing that they don't defecate, and you've cured them with medicine that restricts, and it isn't effective; if they should be restrained with a thread of gold, because threads of silver turn green and rot, but gold never does change. And make sure the thread is not too thin nor too thick, according to the size of the space between the teeth; and if you see to align the teeth, then take the thread and a pair of tweezers between two healthy teeth first, then place the dislocated teeth between your own teeth, if there are one or more, until you feel them properly on the other side; then resume covering up until you covered back that part, and pull your hand subtly and skillfully, until it doesn't move at all; and bind your thread to the root of the tooth so it can't escape. Then cut the dislocated teeth with the thread using tweezers, and assemble them again, and place them between a healthy tooth, and then put it so that it doesn't irritate the tongue; and then leave it like this tightly as long as it can stay, if it loosens or the threads break, you should tighten it with another thread; if stays properly and serves for all its time, and this is the shape of the teeth and the arrangement of two healthy teeth and two dislocated ones, just as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth dislocates, if you put it back in its place, bit by bit, just as we have said; and don't interfere with anything that isn't careful and suffers, and not once does one make the shape of an ox bone tooth, and then place it at the spot where the defect is, and tighten it like what we've said, and stays and serves for so long.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	covering the wound of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	No occasion comes from within the tongue or nature, which we are born with; or by accident of a healing wound; and the procedures are as follows that you work on the mouth for the diseased area, have its head in your healthy hand, and lift the tongue; then cut down the nervous ligament, until the tongue is removed from its position. And if there's stiffness or swelling, which might be due to a sudden wound injury, if you pull off the hook and cut it out completely; and make sure not to let the incision be too deep, for fear of an artery beneath; once completed, then raise your head to pink and cool water, or cold water, then place under the tongue a linen bandage. And soothe the diseased area every night, so that the wounds don't stick together. And if bleeding occurs again, place vinegar over the head; and if this doesn't subside, cauterize with the slow burning cautery, which is well-suited for this task; then continue other treatments until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it's of color or black or hard, such that the patient doesn't feel it when touched, do not touch it for fear of gangrene; and if it turns yellow and shows pus, with moisture present, should you pull off the hook, cut out a thin incision from both sides, and remove it completely. And if the pus continues to come up through your apparatus, place vinegar over it until it's dried, then return to your operation while working with all your strength; then raise your head with cool water and other treatments until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	regarding throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	No matter comes within the throat cavities known as 'godath', and these are properly called the two almonds. And when you treat them, following what we have discussed in division, if they aren't seared, be careful: If there are pus filled lumps of small sensation and fusiform color, don't touch them with a metal instrument at all. And if they are red and their root is large, don't touch them with a metal instrument either, so as not to cause the evacuation of blood; but leave them until they're healed, then you will remove them, or it would break on its own. And if they have a white color and their root is delicate, prepare your tool for application, yet first ensure that the pus filled lump rests and calms down. Then make the patient lie in front of the sun, and let their head be in a healthy position, and let them open their mouth while you hold the servant's hands between their own, and press the tongue over the entire instrument, as described here; and use silver or finely crafted arsenic too, just like knives.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can't you press the tongue with all of this instrument? And when you see pus, take the tincture and insert it into the almond, then pull it upwards more than you can; and remove nothing from the strings with this, then apply to the tool as described here, which seems like a strong force. And both the head is tied together, and one place another, and are very sharp, and is made of iron or arsenic:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this tool present, then use forceps, as depicted here:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And make incisions on both sides, and on each side you name; when you have cut out one of the almonds, then cut the other according to that same manner, and after making the incision gargle the patient with hot, sharp water, and cold water too, and if bleeding starts, then gargle with hot water, or slices of cooked rhubarb, or bay leaves, and similar things, until the wound is healed; then perform the cure until it is healthy; and in no case let other abscesses form in the throat than those two almonds, so cut them accordingly like the two almonds equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman of an abscess that was born inside her throat, one small-sized abscess. I had almost completely closed off the entire throat, so that she could not breathe through the obstructed passage and could neither eat nor drink, dying after one or two days. The abscesses were so high up they were placed in both sides of the neck, with four inches down each side from the throat's entry point. I then hurriedly acted, put an inch of salt into one, followed by pulling out the tube, and a large portion of water; after that, I sewed another part in the other opening near the throat, and made her mouth open while pressing her tongue; afterward, placed the salt inside these abscesses and removed a part from them, only letting a small amount of blood come out. And thus opened up the passage for breathing in the woman's throat, she started drinking water then wine now, not stopping to cut away at that abscess over long periods; and the abscesses grew back immediately, filling the space I had emptied till it became very large; then I treated her gently and cauterized inside the throat: thus did she live without growing worse; and left those parts, and may God do the same for me afterward.
de l’uve	regarding the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the head descends into the eye socket, and it swells up and becomes long, it's called "perpendicular"; and if it's swollen and round, it's called "eye". When it is treated as we have described in the division section, and the treatment isn't helpful, and you notice that the wound has healed, and it feels tender to touch; then it should be handled accordingly. The one that is round assembled and not long; and if its color is red or reddish or black, it should be treated with an incision procedure because there's significant risk involved for the patient. Therefore, when you observe this, according to the method I have mentioned, regarding its size and length, place the patient under the sun so their head faces upwards, press the tongue onto the tool we previously remembered; then insert the needle into the eye, drag it outwards, and apply pressure with two or three tools as described in the incision of four almond-shaped areas. And ensure you don't remove more than the natural limit; for if you take away too much, you could harm voice production and speech ability. After making an incision, use what we have instructed about the incision of four almond-shaped areas, and treat until it heals completely. If there is fear during handling, then it should be treated with a cautery apparatus in that way. The method of cautery usage should be precise. And when the patient's head moves into your healthy section, then press the tongue onto the tool mentioned or detailed within the chapter on cautery equipment, and apply it with lively heat so it is neither too thick nor too thin; and use the movement of this apparatus which was shown here:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let my head have a hair or where I put the medicine, like the movements of a spoon, and place the tool completely with the medicine over the eye socket; and the patient should remain stationary on their side, so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth into the medicine inside, without it descending to the throat or causing irritation; then keep your hand on the medicine and press it over the eye socket for about half an hour, until you see it absorb and the medicine's impacts are relieved; if you notice this, take cotton and wrap it around any tool, moisten the cotton with the medicine, and place the tool completely on the cotton in the wax, until the cotton dries up on the eye socket; and do this often, until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry off, and clean after four or five days. And if you need to reapply the medicine cautery, then do so, and afterwards, wipe around the eye socket with cotton dipped in butter, cleaning that area where there's leftover medicine; rinse with cold water and perform gargling until it is fully healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than incision or the cautery; if it is treated with fumigation like this method, take calamus and juniper and oregano and rue and chamomile and clover and similar herbs, and gather all of them or some of them into one pot, and put water in it, and let it boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and inside the pot have one tool knife according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And make it of silver or lead, and have one of the shoulder blades placed in the mouth against the wound until the vapor rises to the eye via the nose, until the eye is dead; after that repeat often, until the eye dries out, and remember not to do this at the beginning of the coming abscess eruption, for many things happen; and don't perform this method when the abscess is declining. And if this tool isn't present, take a stick and place an eggshell inside your head so that the mouth against the wound isn't too hot; for the eggshell doesn't let the vapor irritate the mouth, and this is a good treatment together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it happens in the throat bone or spine of fish, where nothing occurs; if therefore you are able to do so, then pull out what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with all the tool, so that you see the thing move; and whatever does not open up and is stuck in the throat, it's necessary for you to make the patient vomit like this until the food is cooked in the stomach; by chance if the thing is expelled due to vomiting; or if a piece of sponge, navel, lettuce root, or one piece of dry bread is ingested by the mucus. And tie a string to the sponge and then swallow it afterwards; and when it comes up at the head, if it clears away, and then pull out forcefully; and if it doesn't come out from what we have said, then take one tool of lead according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And prepare the instruments to the throat so that they can enter more lightly into the mouth, and have the head lifted up high above it; and beware not to touch the epiglottis, lest everything goes wrong or pushes the bone inside; and move so that the patient pushes the instrument in its entirety equally until she does it forcefully, as long as it is pushed forcefully.
de la sansue de la gorge	from the saliva of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	No treatment is made of saliva, as I mentioned in the division by medicine cure; and if this doesn't help, then look into the throat of the patient with the sun, because you press their tongue onto the instrument that I've told you. And when you see the saliva, if you remove it with a quarter inch small enough or fine tongs suitable for this task. And if this doesn't work, take a hair, and insert it into the throat where the disease is, then after the hair turns red after one ironing, do this often. And wash the patient's mouth with cold water all day long, then fill a cup of cold water and let them rinse their mouth and pour it down without swallowing, and move it around frequently; and as soon as the saliva feels the water, they defecate.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it doesn't bleed as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafetida, using the tool we've mentioned in the fumigation of the eye. Do this several times because bleeding will occur without scarring. And this way of fumigation is that you take a pot where there are coals and it has a cover pierced in the middle, and at the bottom of that pot are the roots of the tool; then pour your fumigation, put the tip of the cane inside their mouth, seal the mouth so that no fume escapes but goes until it reaches the sinuses; and now the mucus will come out. If it doesn't bleed, restart the fumigation several times; and allow the patient to feel thirsty and eat salty things and such; and don't drink water; then it's necessary for her to leave through this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the tool used to treat the mucus is such that when one can see it, it resembles curved tweezers meant to enter into the throat; and it has the appearance of a doctor's beak, and it has the texture of steel, so whatever she takes doesn't let go; here is its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	This chapter deals with abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	No mention of pus removal are found according to the memory that comes after this from one or another in this book, and they differ in perforation and carving; and it's done in two ways wherein one is like its own appearance, and concerning what has moisture. And the second way is for the areas where they are within the body. For abscesses at the head are different than those at the foundation, and abscesses at the middle meat are different from those that come in joints. Each has their judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if for abscesses one must not pierce them until the body is done according to its maturation. And if there are such that it should be pierced when they have grown and do not mature according to their development, like abscesses below joints. Because when abscesses come from below joints and you leave them until they are rotten inside, by chance if the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, this causes contraction in that limb. Or if the abscess is within the main member, and if you delay piercing it until it's done, it will harm the main member. Or if it is within the foundation, then pierce it when it's done; and one should not pierce a growing abscess without full maturation, except for that which is within the foundation, which rots through completely and lies inside, causing a fistula; and cannot heal properly over a long term.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it must be that you know the time for piercing the abscess which is done according to its maturation, and this is when the pain has subsided, and the departure of fever, and the reduction of pain and redness, and from the movement and firmness of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it must be that you place the piercing area as close or as far as needed from the abscess, and where it opens; and make the piercing at a point along the length of the body, and whether it is in the hands or feet, or joints and nerves and arteries, and all equal areas or places without fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In cases where the joints bend according to that body part. And when abscesses are in the internal flesh, if it's worth mentioning you should let the perforation remain until digestion is fully completed within it, as we said. For if you pierce it beforehand, if it stretches out through the body with its venom and becomes full of a heap of dirt; and by chance hardens the skin and the flesh beneath him. And for any abscesses that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what this member requires. It should be that you remove small abscesses, small protrusions; and in large abscesses, large protrusions, and many openings according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses or it's necessary to cut through its center, and cover it; when it has become as wide as two cloths, and is softened, then it should be done as one does with blisters: and for those that split into three angles, and those in which they cover like the leaf of bay, such as abscesses of angles; and those where a circular cut is made, and other cuts and similar surgical techniques are applied.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those without a head, such as superficial abscesses, it should be that you fully pierce them; and when the abscess is large, and has a lot of pus, if you pierce it, do not remove all the pus at once but remove a part of it. Then seal the abscess until the other end, then leave nothing directly on it; repeat this many times gradually, until all the pus comes out. Similarly, if the patient's immunity is weak or pregnant women, or small children, or elderly and decrepit ones. For there are many times when with the pus discharge, the patient dies, and you don't notice it. Therefore, handle this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscesses, if a wound occurs, check that the wound from the abscess is small; and if it's a simple cut, cover it with lint or old cotton; and if it's large abscesses, and there are many protrusions, then it should be that you sew each one so that they touch each other. And if you have sewn part of the skin in the abscess and sealed it around, then fill it with old cotton or linen rags soaked in moisture, and hold it until the third day; then remove it, and apply ointment to it as long as it is healing.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if bleeding occurs in your operation, then cool and gentle water should be applied and a wet cloth, and place it on the wound many times. And if bleeding persists, then you should provide management and treatment, and use the powders I have mentioned in this book, and if it's near winter, or the location is very nervous, then it should be that you put moistened cloths and pieces of linen on top of vinegar and oil; and if it is a wound, and the area is meaty, then it should be that you place wet pieces of cloth on top of water and oil, or vinegar and cold oil until the third day, as we have said; and then remove and clean the wound, and heal it as needed, as it should be, until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know universally in the treatments of abscesses: now I have told you how one should proceed before the treatments of abscesses, and here begins the chapter.
des soros	of the wounds
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Of the small abscesses that come from the head and are in the form of spots, such as pimples on a girl's face, many have these characteristics. Some are oily like greasy food; others contain moisture like little pustules, and there are some with no doubt that they are veins because they do not behave oppositely to veins. And when cutting into the spot during surgery, use all kinds of tools called 'entromissoire' as follows, this is their form: if it contains moisture, cut deeply from above downwards. And once the moisture has drained out, burn off nothing but the skin that contains this moisture; for if you leave nothing behind, it will heal immediately. Then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment if available; otherwise, use water and salt and apply it to the wound, leaving it until another day; and this heals any overnight soreness. And then repeat dipping the cotton in the same way as before on the second day, and the third day, until you're sure that nothing stays overnight; then treat the wound with ointment suitable for healing, until it is cured. And if the abscess contains one fatty nodule, cut according to this form down the long axis; and cut out all its parts, burn off every part of the skin around it, and apply your entire treatment process on top where it was located; and if the vein causes a reaction opposite to what I've told you, then do what I've instructed after that. And also treat any hard abscess with the same method, cut by the surgeon as I've described.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And when it comes to the incision in relation to a stone wound and moisture, it is easier because there is less blood. And if any of these abscesses or on the head where there's no moisture, then of two such abscesses that I observed or on the head of an elderly woman; I found the abscess as hard, rough and white like sand, and could not break it apart; and if one had cut into it, it would have been treated just like a stone. In other cases where they occur near the head, it's necessary to keep the opening for all days until it depends on its own for bile to come out; and treat them accordingly.
des scrophules	regarding the treatment of scrophula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Many times there occur abscesses in the neck and in the glands, as well as in the armpits, and never at any other place or on a crest, and they are soft and intertwined with each other. And each scrophula is properly within its bony cage, like a nut and an abscess near the head, as we have said; and there are many appearances of these scrophulas. Some contain moisture, while others are wicked and do not wish to obey health. In that case, you will see a good disposition towards treatment, and they resemble the color of the neck, mute from each part and neither close to the throat nor near the artery or in the passage, and not deep; then it is appropriate for you to grasp it from above, and scrape off every part, and take both the two lips of the heart at the veins if needed, as we have said about abscesses near the head; and treat them little by little, and make sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and neither be rash nor go too far ahead, so as not to cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it doesn't allow you to open it, place vitriol broth or any powders that stop blood in the wound; and leave it as long as the abscess is calmed, and the wound has softened, and begins to rot. And when the blood has stopped flowing, return to your work until you complete it; then according to your duty, if there are no small, residual ulcers remaining, remove and cleanse them. And if at the root of the ulcer there's a large vein, it shouldn't be that you cut this ulcer from its root but tie it with a double thick thread, leaving it to naturally fall off without harm; then apply the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then start treating it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you remove the entire ulcer, it's right that you join together the two edges of the wound and stitch them now. There should not be any excess left due to the size of the ulcer; thus, it's necessary for you to focus on removing its root and draining fluid from it before stitching again as explained earlier. The ulcers with excess material should be punctured where they open; and pierce them in a similar manner as previously described, hanging them down, then apply bandages soaked in ointment and such things so that the decay is consumed within; and once the wound has been thoroughly cleaned, start treating it with ointment and all other relevant treatments while keeping it clean.
de squinance	Regarding squint,
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old ones spoke of the art of gullet surgery; but I have never seen anyone do it in our land, and this is written down from their speech.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those with squint, it is necessary that the incision in the throat referred to as "epiglottis" be made; and one should not try this technique because all the vessels and the heart are close to these who have a large amount of mucus either in their mouth or in the throat or near two almond glands.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is within the channel of the lung, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent loss due to strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, it must be done across three or four small cuts through, between the two circles, so that the size of the cut does not involve the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And these joints are capable of undergoing the sectioning of the epiglottis that there is no flesh, and the vessel extends deeply within.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the masters are fearful, it is necessary that they extend the throat skin to the entire length of a finger, then cut through the bone until it reaches the gum; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see anything at all, and then scrape out the tongue, as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it has been demonstrated by the section of the gum artery that bursts through the broken bone, and by the loss of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the time has passed from which one doubts strangulation, gather together the two lips of the wound neatly, and across the entire cut without the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause growth until it is clean.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim, instruct that this should be done until the throat is completely swollen, and the patient's life judged to be at an end, and when there is no further improvement.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Therefore cut into the epiglottis because the patient can't breathe normally, and they are breathing through the wound, and thus you will keep them from dying.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	And because of this, the elderly would instruct to keep the wound open until the disease's malady passes, and it has passed in three or four days.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they instructed to stitch up the wound and treat it, until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a maiden took one knife, and stuck it in her neck, and cut part of the channels from the heart;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to treat her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found the blood that was issuing from it, and indeed, it wasn't accompanied by a severed artery or exit route other than the throat, and the veins bled through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I acted quickly, treated the wound until it was healed;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and did not leave the girl until she had regained her voice, and then returned to her duties afterwards.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I swear by heaven that there is no need for tailoring in the operation of the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	In the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	Cysts of abscesses are called "throat hernia", and they are large abscesses in the color of a blackberry, and there are many in women;
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	and according to two ways: natural and accidents; or naturally has no causality.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidents are according to two ways, of which one seems like fat in us, and the other way seems like an abscess that comes from our arteries;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	And there will be fear, and it is not proper to perform operations outside that in the small ones, and the proof and search must occur throughout all the instruments used.
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it as thin as a new stick, and cannot pierce any vein, then cut through it, as one cuts through wood, and apply the technique to all its parts, if there is even a hint of it.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And search thoroughly from start, and treat as it should be treated until it is completely healed.
des nous	from the bones
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many ways exist for us, so I will say all the similarities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And it is fitting that I should mention all the differences that exist between us and the outcome.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that issue is characterized by heat and fever lasting until the body's flushes have passed and putrefaction has occurred; then, the fever and heat settle.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the new one, there is no heat, fever, or pain, and it contains a single pus, which is its own sack and varies in size according to the color of the body, and starts off like an apple, and becomes swollen;
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	And they depend on two appearances, or greasiness, or moistness, and little color change as I have described in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to the treatment of new injuries, it is necessary that you first inspect and inquire about all the tool which is called 'the adjuster', according to its shape or chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the method of inspecting the abscesses in wounds is that you remove as much moisture as you find inside the abscess, and twist your fingers slightly and gradually, until you know that the tools have reached the center, then do it according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then remove the adjuster tool, and be careful not to let it break.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture is released, whether it has this color or not, if it's made like I said for other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if after the incision no moisture comes out, know that it's fatty, if then you make a cross cut and pinch it, take it lightly with pincers, and slightly scrape each side. Then remove the coat where it lies, so you can take it away cleanly with the nut;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot take it out clean, then take it piece by piece so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything is left behind, it will return to us many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if it stays for a little while, and the patient does not suffer, then fill the wound with some corrosive powders that cause irritation, and restrain the wound, and place things that soothe abscesses in hot water, and treat other treatments until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if it hurts greatly, then cover the wound with two of his mouth's lips, and treat those who are in pain due to bleeding.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein is too large or another condition requires urgency and you need to treat it with vinegar poultice, let it remain for one or two days or three, until the wound discharges pus, then rest in hot blood; afterwards return to treating where he has been exposed to the new.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Know these forms of instruments for internal use, and they are in three ways: large, medium, and small; and if there are four squares which are called "albaret", and one called "breb", and there are also in three ways: large, medium, and small, to encircle the abscesses of fistulas;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	And they are also like needles from which one removes the thorns, and are of lemon citrine, or iron, or silver, and gold yellow ones are valued more than black lead for enclosing pus pockets;
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	And there are three ways: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The shapes of the pins are like little images, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and if there are two bumps on the pins in three different ways, too;
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	And if the pins have two bumps, they are also in three ways; and if there are pins with two bumps, and single-bumped pins, and these are all in three ways; and all of this is necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of this one that they make to be cutting, and there are those who do not cut force from both sides, whom we burn the flesh, for in such cases one does not encounter a vein or nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And these introducers have their handles restored to the hand, so that the patient does not notice them during the opening of abscesses;
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	And there are three ways: large, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and one does not use much force only in the leg muscles, such as legs and arms, nipples, and similar body parts.
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	And no other small tool is ever made, resembling whips of gallstones, according to this form, on which one stops the blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And it is placed in the healthy part of the body, at the junctions of veins and arteries, and never according to this large form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	None of the men swell their nipples when they begin to become corrupt, until they seem like nipples of women;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	And remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wishes to cure them should follow this method described by line B until .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then scrape off the fat, and fill the wound with an ointment that encourages new flesh to grow, then join together both edges of the wound for stitching, and treat it until it heals.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	And if the belly sags down and is flattened due to its size, just like it happens in women, cut it into two sections above, making two similar incisions;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	From which one holds to the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line B until this line G;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then scrape off the skin that is between the two edges, and remove the fat, and apply the treatment that we have described for stitching and powders, and what is necessary in the healing process, until it heals.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	And if it isn't clean, or if the incision hasn't been completed, because the patient doesn't want to rest, or due to blood flow, it is necessary that you fill the wound with wet cotton in a corrosive dressing;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	And let it grow until it starts to chew and move again, then clean it as long as it is sanitized.
des apostemes des asselles	from abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Abscesses that originate in the armpits are manners of hard scrofulas where there are nodes, and if there are any containing moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture should be cut according to this shape, from line b. up to line .g:

Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is cut and the skin is sewn up above it, many times one will find an abscess. et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if one knows this when it's due to an artery, then the abscesses are long and straight.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when you feel it with your fingers, if you sense resistance; and when it's due to a vein, then there are clear protrusions;
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it's folly to cover this abscess, and likewise when it is under the axilla and under the elbow, and around the neck, and in other parts of the body, and they are very large.

puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	Then work on the size of ounces, and cleanly separate the artery from the meshes, until it is exposed;

des apostemes des ners	Of abscesses of nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also like abscesses appearing in arteries and veins, they appear on nerves when they are cut or due to too much work, and similar things.

des grosses boces pendans	Of large boils hanging down

dou chancre	treat the gangrene
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed in the division the appearances of gangrene, and how to handle it with medicine, and how to avoid iron treatment; we shall explain that gangrene appears within the flesh, requiring great caution during its treatment. The old ones say that when gangrene is found on skin or parts you can remove, such as breast gangrene, in cooking areas, and similar spots, one should remove everything when it's just starting. But for large and old gangrene, approaching it doesn't work; I never knew anyone to be cured by it, nor did anyone else before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when it's in a place you can remove, as we have said, the procedure is to cleanse the patient of black bile on all sides. Then have the surgeon drain if there's obvious fullness, then prepare for surgery by thoroughly cleaning out the affected area. Next, scrape out or cut away gangrene from everywhere and clear it completely with nothing left behind; let the blood flow freely until you've wiped your hand clean over it or any other surface. If bleeding contradicts the incision made in an artery or vein, cauterize so that the wound is fully dry. Then apply another treatment once it's healed.
