et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	And they do not appear according to this reason among those who are delicate, and have wet bodies and veins that respond.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see the treatment of this illness, and if the patient feels pain from it, open them as we have said if they show signs of it.
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	If you see that the wind (here likely referring to air or breath) is escaping both up and down quickly, then hold this constriction until the disturbance of the wind in its place subsides.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	And apply the cautery to it; and if you do not see it working on your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	If one is treating a case of wind expulsion issues, such as stinking pills, venomous pill of the viper, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, depending on their appearance and according to the location of their impact on the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is such that there are those with large points, and small ones, and barbed, and soldered;
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	And concerning those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those where there are fragments;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	And the one who urinates in no member but does so according to two ways: or in the main body it dribbles,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	as with the brain, heart, liver, kidneys, lungs, intestines, bladder, and other similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	And when she urinates in no part of these members, then the signs of death, which I will tell you later, become evident to you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	If it is necessary for you to proceed with the extraction of this arrow, because death comes after in various dispositions;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And when that bad sign does not become apparent, and the arrow is not entirely out, if you pull it, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And when that brain sign occurs when the arrow hits and pierces the bone, and there is a sudden rush of fluid from the head,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And when blindness and numbness occur along with inversion and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and muscle spasm and confusion in understanding, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	And perhaps it affects the nostrils or the ears; and sometimes it causes loss of speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	And there is a moist white swelling resembling a boil, and in that boil also like burnt meat;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And if this sign appears, hold onto the treatment, and pull out the arrow if it hasn't been removed.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it's drawn or retracted is that it is close to the left breast, and also feels like it might be embedded in something hard, not empty;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And by chance the heart also beats as do the rabbits, and during black blood loss, and brings on coldness and cold sweat, and fainting:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	So know that death is near.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that never leaves its path is when blood spurts from the wound without foam, and the throat swells up, and the patient's face changes color, and they sigh loudly while their body grows cold.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow stops inside the leg's fur, it is located below the small ribs; and there is great bleeding and great pain and sighing; and all limbs from the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow or stomach penetrates it, perchance something of the undigested meat comes from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow or stomach pierces it, and if there is no meat in the intestines after jumping from the wound, then there's no hope for treatment, nor extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow penetrates into the bladder, and urine flows out and escapes after jumping from the wound, and patients feel intense pain: know that this injury is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other body parts, such as the limbs (including arms and legs), neck, throat, shoulder, elbow, back, spine, knees, and feet, as well as any similar parts, are safe according to various positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When an arrow is in the nerve or artery and it isn't venomous, as I will tell you that this happened to me, because what you did was different.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened in one instance where an arrow struck the right shoulder at the root of the neck:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried to pierce it, and from the other side through the fatty tissue of the ear, causing no sensation.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And pierced with an arrow that struck in the fat near the eye below the paper sheet.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	And the arrow was returned, and one could not reach even its tip to the shaft,
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And the arrow was long as a Turkish bow, about one hand's width without an ear; the patient was sound, and he suffered no ill accidents.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I shot an arrow from the throat to a Christian, and the arrow had ears for this one: Arab style.
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I held my breath, and kept it as long as I shot it, and the Christian was sound.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And shoot an arrow through one's body, if it was stuck in their back or belly, and thought that they would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and after it had been over thirty days, if it did not change its position;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut through the arrow, set the instrument, and forcefully pulled it out, without any bad incident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you find one who was hit by an arrow in their back or front, and the wound has healed over;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	And the arrow stays within, not returning to its natural position,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And finds no harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And to another man, who was struck in his face by an arrow, and had the wound stitched up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And it was like that, causing him such great pain; and there were other similar situations.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And when you shoot an arrow from half a home distance to the king's prince, where it gets stuck halfway in his nose,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was slightly tilted towards the right side; and the arrow was fully inserted.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to treat it after it had been stuck for three days. I found the wound very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I tried everything with my subtle instrument, but did not feel any change;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	And he felt pain and discomfort around his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow.
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on his head a restorative plaster, because the hair did not swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw the arrowhead in the hair.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I placed a plaster on for many days, and cleansed the wound directly, then kept the patient suffering long thereafter.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	Until he felt the arrow passing through his nose; and I told him about it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I placed a corrosive antiseptic on the wound for many days until it was opened.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	And I tested it, and felt the tip of the arrow as it was passing through to the other side;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then adjust in the opening of the wound through this medicament, until I clearly saw the head of the arrow;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and pierced well to the inner ends for three months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	then I separated as much of the wound so that my forceps could touch both sides, and applied it from one side to the other, but it could not come out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	therefore I did not stop refining and devising ways of instruments, until I managed to use two well-made forceps for it for one day;
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	According to how its form will come at the end of this chapter, as long as I handle it, and I shall restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the judges decide that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I will thus restore it, and then suture the wound, and the patient's injuries will be completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	So I told you about the quality of extracting some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	If you place your treatment on what I do not say, because books cannot take everything into account;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but the wise masters compare well to small matters, and concerning what is current and lacking,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	True to new work, and a ninth instrument, for the removal of foreign things that happen in this craft.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not lie in the limbs where they are stuck according to two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	By means of the arm where they enter, or from another side;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	And that which enters by the arrow's wound when it enters in their flesh, this is the shaft within them, and now it enters only once.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not enter now, let her stay until the flesh is fully healed inside, and wait for its release;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And likewise if it's stuck in the bone, and cannot come out, let her stay like that for a few days, and remove it each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it jumps, and if it does not jump, if you pierce through all with one thin hole, as long as the hair in between is widened, and then insert.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow has been stuck into the skull bone, and goes up until one of the brain cavities,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	And some of the accidents that I have mentioned appear to the patient: if they do not remove it but leave it until certain days after, and then it becomes equal.
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	because if the arrow has come up to the braincase, this is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is merely stuck in the bone alone, not reaching all the way through,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and remains for some days without any bad incident, provided that the extraction tool works well.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it's so deeply stuck and cannot come out at all, then use internal threads such as I have instructed you; then treat the wound until it is clean.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow has been returned to inside the body so that we cannot see it, then search thoroughly for all its parts;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel it, guide it with no suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot do it due to the tightness of the wound, and because of the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone, nerve or vein, so you make it as long as the wound becomes large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if there are holes in the arrow where it holds,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if you have a bone that's stuck for half an inch, you should know how to remove it.
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the arrowhead's ears until you can draw blood from it;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	Be subtle so that you do not break the arrow but draw blood more forcefully from it.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you can't do it in one go, leave it until its entire length is rotted away by maggots, then try to pull it out, as extraction requires effort.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if blood flow opposes you, then apply what we have instructed regarding treatment as described in our chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and beware of incising near nerves and veins, and make the cut so that you can extract the arrow without risk,
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	either quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient in the position they were in before the arrow struck them.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	because it's best for them to be as comfortable as possible, and if you can't do that, place them according to what the medical sign shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another side, or if it exposes any part of it, or if the skin is swollen in such a place that one sees or feels it distinctly:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	So grasp at the arrow from above, as long as the tongs can take hold of it, and then pull it out: if it jumps suddenly.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if she is held in the bone, twist your hand round as long as she enters the bone and widens the bone, then pull her out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if she cannot come out, leave her there still, and start extracting again until she comes out;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	And if there is an arrow involved, hold it at the entire shaft;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	And if it's bone, and you need to administer thrusting (a method of treatment), then use the instrument that's suitable for bones.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the tip of the arrow enters the channel of the tool; and then apply force,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is stuck, use another tool with an entering tip to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is encircled, it must be that you grasp all the flesh inside or where I come in, if you can,
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as it becomes necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow hits or pierces the belly or bladder or ribs, and it is close to doing damage, and you can reach it, then you should grasp it up; if you can.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And watch over not to cover the vein and the nerve, and then remove it, and afterwards suture the wound; that is the task.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And keep the treatment until it has healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pincers used for arrows is similar to the tip of a bird's beak, and here is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the hair on the head is also like the feathers of a bird,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	for pushing at the tip of the arrow, as this is its form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the pliers for pushing and pulling as such is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	from the horns of common veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	The veins from which we cleanse are thirty-one, of which there is sixteen for the head.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	This means: Two small ones that are behind the ears, they are called the "two herbs".
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	And the two arteries that are in the two temples visible;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	And two veins that are in the two eyelids of the two eyes, they are called "aspires";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	And the vein that is within the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the head near the nose;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two jugulars which are at the collarbone;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are in the cheeks above the mouth, and these are the veins which are called 'aughershire';
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that run along the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins which are commonly treated are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the cephalic vein, and it starts from the left side of the chest, and they call it 'the common vein' or 'vein of the head';
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	And the middle one is called 'fast' and is made up of the cephalic and basilic veins,
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	And they call it 'the vein of the heart'; and the basilic either is from or to the right side of the chest,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	And they call this condition "the vein of the belly", and it's above the pubis,
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and that which is healed, whose opening becomes clearly visible at the scrotum.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the salvation tool is the vein located between the index finger and the ring finger, and it has a diameter of two fingers;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	And in the leg and where the patella is, there are three veins: one of which is below the knee on the left side of the body,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	And this is the second sentence which is at the ankle bone on the right side; and this vein, which is called 'nurse', is in the ankle of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	And in the other leg are three veins next to those ones.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The health of the veins that are after the ears helps with fevers and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	And the qualities of a healer, as I tell you, it is so that you heal the head of the patient.
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	And rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then pinch the patient's neck at the base of their head.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until you see the two veins behind the ears under the second ear to the forehead:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	place your hand there, and where you feel the pulse under your hand, if it beats strongly.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	Then take the lancet, and hold the needle right above the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand all the way up to the vein above.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	And cut and loosen the skin and the vein well two inches deep, and let blood come out as long as you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then hold and bind it until it heals;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already discussed the incision and the cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The healing of the two arteries that are in the temples, if it resembles an old embolism,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	And indeed, and to the eyes accustomed, and on the body of feverous tears, to the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And that quality of the surgeon is such as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	And it happens that the patient strains their throat until both two veins are clearly visible;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the pulse twice on each side, and then gives judgement on it;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	Then lift your hand above the vein near your elbow and hold the scalpel steadily,
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and lift the vein at the top, and the flap, just like you did in other veins, and let out the blood according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then release the hair, and place your thumb on the vein for an hour, then put cotton there;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	And then the wound forms, and you should leave it until it heals; and we have spoken about this before in terms of its care and removal, or beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The vein in the forehead heals just as much as the temple vein when it comes to diseases of old like migraines and hives;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And its quality is that the patient constrains his neck by twisting, until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the tool called "awl", which has this shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the tip on the vein, or extend your hand, or another thing, and let out blood according to the amount you see.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then release the neck of the patient, and tie the vein as long as it is healthy and without any operation has not left a broad wound.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Always remember, it is not right for the flames to be too close; and the skin should be cut diagonally because the bone is nearby. By chance, they may break the flames when they are subtle.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The incision for the two veins that are in the eye sockets aids the eyes, and at the nose, and around the mouth, and at the ear canal, and for diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the quality of their healing is such that the patient twists his neck by binding a certain ligament, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then the healing occurs, and so the wound passes through, somewhat along the length of a small flame somewhat wide, for there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are thin, suppose they break; then pour blood, as much as you need, and then cover with cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The healing of the vein near the nose is good for fever, and for hot baths, and for stomach illnesses,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	as when there is headache and heat coming to the face, and indeed when she is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and it is that the sick person so constrains her throat that they pinch her nose with their left hand.
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take a subtle flame and insert it between the two nostrils into the space inside the lip.
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	for the mouth does not open properly yet, and the operation will now begin to correct;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	And do not proceed too hastily with this, adjust your treatment according to necessity then leave them alone for a night, because it is very quickly restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and it takes the form of flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The health of two gallbladders helps with constriction of the bile ducts and the beginning of mixers, and much disease, and in putridity, and corrosion, and herpes, and emesis;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of health is such that diseases are stretched in both their necks from one to the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	And may the masters being on top of the head of the patient, and the patients lie flat on one side for an hour,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	Then open the vein as long as somewhat wider, then drain the blood moderately, or as much as is needed;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	Then make another incision in the other vein, then release the knot, and restrain moderately the veins.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	That the patient doesn't strangle themselves; and leaves them until morning, so that the wound heals.
De la sainie des leivres	Regarding the healing of ears
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The care of veins in the mouth aids in collection within the mouth, and contributes to gum decay, and splits in lips, and nosebleeds and internal bleeding.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of this care involves making the patient sit before you, and supporting their neck as I have described;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	Then turn the mouth, and look at these two veins, one is on the right lip and the other on the left.
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and you can recognize them by their blackness, and by the fact that inside they contain small black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	Now handle both of them, and if you do not know which one, and you are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	If you handle the larger one of each part, and do likewise with both veins above and below, because it is the same method.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the health of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The health of the veins located on the tongue aids after the head's health, and this is done by constricting the throat. It also deals with diseases of the eyelid, and diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the quality of a healthy person is such that when their body parts are examined with the sun shining on them and they move their tongue, one can see black veins on both sides:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Then indeed both of them are healthy, and do not extend too far down; because there are the arteries beneath.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of a cut, which are generally healed, are treated according to two methods:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or by applying a broad, smoky heat from one type of flame (like that from animal fat), or from a fine olive oil if it's like the blades of a knife, and these are called 'anisel'.
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are broad or fine depending on the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the mirtin flame is very well known, and it's quite wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it requires to open veins filled with large visible blood clots, and those containing large amounts of thick blood.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the shape of olive oil flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it's more refined and pointed, used to heal fine veins, or one with fine yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The healing of the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps with illnesses that occur in the throat, and neck, and stomach, and abdomen;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is necessary for the surgeon to heal skillfully, and to beware of the artery which is nearby.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and bleeding occurs, it is necessary for him to stop it, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and must not be held by the flame, but cut in such a way that it resembles a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica does not open clearly, you should extract it and change to another one;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	You want no blood from him, or you release it through his arm under him. It becomes clear clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And the incision on fire beforehand, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you know where to make the wound heal, it is necessary that you straighten the arm, touching the place until you find the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	Then mark where to cut, and then bind the arm, making a cut on the vein as we have said before.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And make sure you do not cut into the artery when you see the limb swell, for this is from the artery: hear then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it bulging up as high as a child's urine, and the veins are red and subtle, know that these are veins from the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hasten then, place your finger for a while, then remove your finger when the bleeding stops, as has often happened;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	Fasten his arm and leave it like this, don't move the patient's limbs; stay ready for fear, don't move until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the wound is not bleeding, and you need to do so, and the medicine is not at hand, if you open the artery when it opens, because the head of the body withdraws; and stop the bleeding on the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a bark from a broomstick, and cut it, and take one of the halves and bind it well up to the other side.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If the wound stops bleeding, that's good; if not, apply it as we have said, with powders that stop the blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the remedies should not be applied in more than a few locations for the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm's joint.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The treatment of blood flow takes place in the middle where she aids in the treatment of blood near the head above, and the heart below.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	Because it is composed of the basilica and cephalic parts, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	And it is important for the surgeon to be aware of the nerve that's located there, and if he doesn't go far enough, and he finds the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	And it inflames and damages health, and in case of accident, can't heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any of them due to its subtlety, then you should cut the patient near the tool; and listen for the sound of the nerve with your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, make the incision long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The treatment for headache helps, as it draws blood from the head, and assists with the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is advisable to treat with the oil flame or with the mint flame, as this is the safest of all veins, because there is neither beside the nerve nor artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Always, it's necessary to seek the lightest method, and one should not be troubled if they have to try once more, then retry.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And sometimes, swelling occurs in certain limbs after the first attempt, but one should not be troubled by this.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health depends on your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you need to know about surgery is that health is managed through means only to preserve health,
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	And to avoid future illnesses;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and let the healing take place in one of the three veins that are or cut: namely, the cephalic, the facial, and the basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and let healing begin at the start of prayers on one's knees, and in autumn and after meals during winter, when the sign of fullness is observed;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and let healing begin on the first or third day, after two or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The healing that is administered for illnesses does not have a set time, but only when need arises during the day or in terms of sustenance, at all times and in every situation;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And it is not suitable for a surgeon to heal children until the age of 13 years, nor women who are pregnant for only one quarter of a month up until seven weeks.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	And it is not suitable for surgeons to heal the elderly who have surpassed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when any wish to be treated, in whatever manner it may be, if it is necessary that they evacuate their intestines with a gentle cathartic.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	If there is a bit of fat retained, so that the veins pull out excesses from the intestines harmful to the main limbs;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	Neither does one recover from those who are too full of meat, nor those who are drunk, until they are strong, or have dropsy;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	And if one is well informed about the healer after colic passion, and vomiting, and bowel loosening, and frequent urination in women, and work, staying awake and exercising, as well as whatever consumes the strength, or due to something from the arm or injury;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then make subtle the fluids, if they are excessive through meat and drinks and medicine, provided you have the means;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	Then within or during a bath, if no thing breaks outwards, to thin out the blood,
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and heal her of the vein from below up to the middle third, as we said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and guard that day from labor, pain, and excess, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and tie yourself and rejoice, and let the nurse be higher than whom you are being healed, and rub your arm twice or three times.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	Then adjust the tie above moderately, for when it is too tight or too loose, it cannot correct itself without;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub your arm with your hands until the veins swell up and you can feel them;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then moisten the wick with a little of old oil flame, then place your left hand's index finger on that vein slightly above the elbow;
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not burn or rupture from being hit.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that flow as cords on the bowyer, and there are such that are full of wind,
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when put over the flame, they retract towards the flame, and cannot open the vein, thus one is of those;
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if it opens the vein, then the wound is too narrow, for in such cases, the bowyers must be skilled in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens for the first time, it's good; if not, try again a little around that spot or quickly, as long as his arm isn't swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the limbs are swollen, and the veins appear, let it rest for one or two days, and do not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	By chance pus-filled blisters may come out; do not enter water, then start the cleaning if it pleases her.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if the pus pocket is small, or if there's a slight hole and you doubt that it doesn't drain as much blood as you see, if you pierce this pocket itself all the way to the root;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And let the wound heal a bit faster, so that the limbs swell; because this happens many times, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see that the body swells, if you do not restart the healing process, and apply a little of olive oil, because it alleviates the body's pain from blood, and makes the oil stick in this area of the body.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus apply the olive oil to each healing you do on veins, to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and similarly apply vinegar and wine when you put them on the body; if the oil is too thick, it separates from the blood.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And when there comes about large abscesses, which occur often, just as when healing has not been completed, especially if the opening of the vein is small.
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	If you are prepared, place on the limb a sponge moistened with water and wine for an hour and then remove it.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	It is necessary that you perform this after the blood has flowed from the vein, and if it stays in place for several days without any blackness or greenness, then it does not harm it.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see so, place on it something of myrrh or aloes, ground and made into a juice from comfrey, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	Many times pus and appearance of healing were seen in the cure of the basilica: so place your hand there, and if you find the limb soft to the pressure of your hand, this indicates an unhealthy condition.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, you should not apply anything from what we have discussed here, for fear of harming the artery; but have it properly plastered dry to harden the area, then proceed with another treatment until it heals.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And for each one give blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	And if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see that it's large, let it continue flowing until it thins out; and if it's too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And for the one who is full and free, needing blood extraction, it's necessary to make the wound larger and have wide flames.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for him who is weak, do the opposite, and it suits better to serve him with small and frequent doses, and he must be cured by cutting across, not straight.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this way of treatment saves from the spreading of blood and the entrapment of nerves, and is preferable to prolonged rather than broad cutting.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for the patient whose body needs surgery, you should give them moist bread in the juice of pomegranate apples; if they are heated, let them drink three or four times this mixture.

et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use the other things that we have said in the section or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of veins.

et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put on one finger's breadth of salt immersed in water, and gently press it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it alone and do not squeeze it, until the abscess subsides.

Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is clean at its point of connection with the main vein because it is separate from the neck vein due to its composition.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method of cleansing involves having the patient soak their hand in hot water until the veins become red.

Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The treatment of the right hand is equivalent to the disease of the mouse, and do everything as I have told you for the left.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The treatment of the stomach suits all diseases that exist in the body,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	Like diseases of the stomach, and retention of flowers (possible reference to herbal medicine), and disease of the bladder, and in old legs and feet, and similar illnesses.

ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt about nerves, as we have said before, and do similarly with the other leg equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The veins of the sciatic region are at the ankle bone, and their health corresponds to the pain in the hip; when it is due to blood congestion.

car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	for otherwise the vein does not open; and if it does open, heal it in all ways that you can, and across;

et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And do such a thing with the blood until you see it, then loosen the tie and put on cotton to press; she is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Pleas note that "des sainies de ventouse" in Old French refers to treatments involving suction cups (like using a suction cup for medical purposes). But it's an obsolete term and isn't directly translatable into modern English language. This might be referring to bloodletting, or the practice of extracting blood from patients as a form of treatment which was common before modern medicine times. In essence, this could refer to procedures like leech therapy (where leeches are used to suck out blood) or the use of suction cups in medical practices.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses are made from horns, or spiders, or leeches; and suction cupping is done in two ways: either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this ventilation which can cause injury is done in two ways: or it can be at all fires, or with fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and the ventilation that is done by causing injury and blood extraction occurs in twelve ways in one's body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	because some affects the entire head area; and others are situated within the neck.
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two others on both sides of the neck; and the sucking action under the chin.
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the suction tool for the two shoulders; and the suction tool on the boils;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the suction cups for the two arms; and the suction cups for the two legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the suction cups for the ankles; and the suction tool does not treat of blood, but rather small veins that are scattered in the flesh,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and because of this I did not weaken myself, just as one would treat with a vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And it should not be administered, nor with any fire or without fire, in any illness that comes from overfullness, until all the body is drained.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if suction is necessary due to diseases or out of habit, we should perform it every hour at the beginning of each month, or at its end, and continuously during any period.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are those who, when they need to suction, start weighing after much effort;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and if for such individuals there is congestion and redness in their face, and on their head, and at the neck, and discomfort in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	And those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have fainted, and are coughing up blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if there are such things that worry them, and they see by their noses blood and nostrils and death-like things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially at the beginning of each month, we command to drink after three hours during the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The treatment of the nose helps with inflammation in the head... bringing the eyes, and it is not right that this should be done after the elimination of everything from the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	And this ventilation is at the location of the head's health,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And it is not suitable for those with a cold constitution, or who have diarrhea, because this causes them much harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And it is also not good for someone to use it if they suffer from cold conditions or diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And whoever uses it often becomes forgetful, and due to this, it's necessary to place the suction cup slightly further down by the suspicion of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	Ventilation near the neck is located beneath the head and the basilica, and for this reason it is beneficial to tighten below the elbows.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and in cutting through the channel of the pulmonary artery, and everywhere, and in replenishment;

And it is in the place of the healing of the basilica; and you should instruct the healer to extend their hand upon putting it, not to touch the artery, and not to wait for blood to appear.

The ventilation under the chin corresponds to mouth diseases, and gum decay, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of the healing of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Ventilation under the shoulders corresponds to disease brought about by heat and congestion.

Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup that is on the buttocks is effective for bleeding from the bottom and diseases around it. Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The leg suction cups are applied directly because they draw blood from the entire body and are beneficial for old pains in the kidneys, bladder and uterus, as well as reducing swelling; they are located at two shin points and the ankles, and all the while they weaken the body after long use, leading to pale complexion in various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method for using the suction cup is as follows: place it initially in an empty state and apply continuous suction. Quickly put it on the wound, move it evenly, and keep doing this action without stopping until you see the area turn red and swell. Then remove it, and reapply the suction cups; take care of the position of the organs because there are those with thick skin and clear pores: for these, one must pierce once only, make broad incisions, and go somewhat deep; suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the lump is large, it might require two piercings: once to subdue the path of thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the lump is very dense, it might require a third piercing; and when we wish to extract a little blood at a time, we should only pierce once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we wish to remove some blood, we often reinitiate it; and if the heart is weak, we firmly press down on it, and the ends are such that they pierce through instantly.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And it is necessary for one who has thick skin and hardness, and those with tight pores, that you grease the hands with sucking cups from which an opening is seen and dissolving:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it's in the form of a bluish oil or an almond sweet oil, or an oil from the seeds of cucumber;

et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it must be done when he should be suctioned and when he has been suctioned.

Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The suction cups that are placed to cause irritation are those placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and in gout, and on the abdomen and uterus, and kidneys, and hip, because this body does not tolerate being pricked by needles on wounds.

As with ailments of the tears in, and in such manner we make the suction cup filled with hot water, or with water that has cooked suitable herbs for this purpose.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup used heated like this is:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And has two and a half spans in width, and at its center it is hollow halfway through, so as to be able to stick out like one would when piercing with a needle,

et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	And there is in the middle a rod across of an araignee or iron, for placing a candle taken hold.
