car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the suction cups for children are different from those for adults, and the thin ones differ from the fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one must place this suction cup thus on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	Take the wax stick or one thread, and place it inside the suction cup over the foreskin which is under the suction cup.
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	Let the heat reach to the bottom of the suction cup so that it doesn't burn the penis;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	Then place it on the member and you should do so at the point that we have mentioned. So when one wants to use it, if heat goes up, and removes the suction cup;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	Apply the thread in the same manner as described before, and repeat this often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the suction cup method used in pleurisy disease, during all stages of fever, there is neither a sharp nor a dull pain, and it is administered only when the body is full of water, being placed solely on the member.
et c’est li forme:	and this is its shape:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Wounds are not treated with suction cups except in limbs where one cannot place suction cups due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar areas;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and on the naked skin of a wound, like in elbows or knees, and other similar areas;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	And if you find veins that are in clear water without inflammation when they are clean, take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and place them in lukewarm water until they become accustomed and have nothing in their abdomens;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	then use bloodletting and suction cups, then rub the limb until it turns red, and place the veins on it.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and start to ache, if there's a place where you can put suction cups, do so, because this helps very little afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not so, raise the patient first with solid help, then with liquid aid, quite well, then proceed to incision.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the patient dies too soon after the movement of the joints, due to bleeding. Apply one liter of cold water in linen cloth, and place it upon them, until the veins are swollen;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if there are multiple veins, apply powdered vitriol or garlic, and similar substances, until the veins become swollen.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	Or put half a peeled pea on the patient's skin and leave it until they heat up on the body, this will stop bleeding now.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you need more knowledge, take other instructions.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the veins are unwilling to be taken, rub with a fresh blood source, or insert an awl until blood begins to flow.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	Then place them and soon as they feel the blood, you stir them;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see that they are bleeding, sprinkle a little myrrh and flour on them, or ash, they will bleed now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and restoring and resetting of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know this, dear child, that the leaves of this chapter have been turned by you, and you saw nothing from the old books, nor did anyone ever read a letter of it;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason, the knowledge has been taken away from our land, because I have never found anyone good in this regard;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I know nothing of this, for by the knowledge of old books, or with which I have studied so much that I dealt with the art, and through experimentation, and through my life's habit;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	And I have described in this chapter what is contained, and abbreviated it at the end, and clearly shown the shapes of the instruments that are used, as I did in these two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is necessary that we outline or provide an introduction to this book containing the essence of knowledge and the chapters where the wise person applies their understanding, staying true to reality. So that those who have experienced it may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I state that when any fracture or dislocation or twists or contusions occur to anything, it is necessary for you to quickly treat the patient on both sides and parts, without allowing anything bad to happen, such as weakness in body, children, or elderly individuals;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the place where you're tightening is too tight, or too cold; and consume cold meats, this means cold cuts, and liver and venison meat, and do not drink wine, nor consume any fatty foods. Do not fill up with too much meat that fills veins with blood, until you doubt of an abscess forming hotly, or spreading of matter in the limb; if the patient feels better according to their initial treatment as they have been using it.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that you feed the patient with meats that cause significant nourishment, or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and onions, and chestnuts, and pies, and veal spleen, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For such nourishment leads to movement and more quickly heals the breakage.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of old and weak people cannot be healed or joined properly according to their nature due to the drying out of limbs, nor those also who are too tender, such as the bones of young children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but take care, reset the broken bone. I.e., firmly apply and join the limb together, as long as it strengthens just as it was before; and do not rush with his work, for this requires feeding on large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that breaks come in various ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a break at the neck is different from a break at the knee or leg, and in this chapter I will tell you all ways of breaking.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are breaks leading to war, and others through preparation, as with the size of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And in cases of injury along with breaks, and breaks resulting from a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each way has its own method, and its proper tool for restoration, according to what memory brings to its place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and the break of the bone is known by the fact that the limb is twisted, and opens well through the skin, and hurts when pressure is applied to it;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when there is no twisting or deformation of the joint, and the patient does not feel great pain, should there be no breakage;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can well have twisting, or a crack, or small breakage.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not suitable for you to move it by hand, but apply the remedies that come next, and then gently constrain it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the break that went in the arm, and are two parts out of joint, it is suitable for you to put them at an equal point, thus that abscesses have to be worn inside or outside;
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	And if abscesses are pus-filled, if he leaves them for no day, until the abscess becomes calm;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then place them evenly with what you can lightly and wisely do, knowing that the restoration of this is easier than the restorations when he has pieces; then extract it, as is fitting after this.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if within the bone are broken pieces, if they have been separated by two parts, whether it's hands or feet, or at your hand if it's a small member, or by two strings, or by one string and at your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and place the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the injured member are healed, you can gradually reintroduce additions into their places as long as you can, and remember to ensure that in your work there is no harm or pain inflicted upon the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And adjust well the two shoulder joints of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it well with your hand if you think it's not quite right: if you treat it beautifully, and don't strain it too much, don't press it as those who bring it about by their method of pus evacuation and muscle contraction do to the limb, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limbs are ready, carefully restrain the patient so they do not move, whether awake or asleep, while turning or in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	Make sure that the limbs are securely fastened so that there is no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, it is not properly adjusted, and it must be placed in an appropriate position so that he does not feel any pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and keep it straightly set, ensuring no twisting occurs when you reset it;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the limb broken is as I told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	You know that limbs broken are diverse in smallness and largeness, and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small limbs such as arms and legs and alike; it is necessary to wrap them in soft and fine linen cloths.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	And those that are larger, such as the chest and thighs: it is necessary to wrap them in a broad and hard bandage. This wide bandage embraces all of the large limb, and constrains it evenly from all sides, ensuring there is no unevenness;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then bind them with lighter bandages, perhaps three times or four according to the limb, and hold your hand on for a moment all across the bandage. et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And soften the bandage gradually and gradually, until you have made a large part of the healthy area, then take another bandage and return around it to the wounded limb;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then return to the part of breaking and slightly squeeze it, not too hard nor too gently, as we have said in the first instruction above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place the twisted linen bands or cloths between them until they are evenly matched in size, then secure everything by tying it with an additional band of cloth. And place your well-made stars on top; if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there's swelling or pus, then place something soothing for abscesses on top, and that relieves the swelling, and leaves it like this for a few days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then apply pressure to the stars, and they should be half as wide as a small cane or stick, or made from what is used to make sticks, or from palm leaves, and they should be shaped like this:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But it is necessary that the hot iron used on the burn mark outsize slightly more than the others.

puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then hold it on the hot irons in the same way you did with the first application, then bind an additional thread over it, just as you did on the burn mark.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	make it tighter, but not too tight; and it is necessary that the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, and should be made of soft linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the threads are thick, as I have wished for works of hemp that twist their lines together, and this is great error, because the line cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it does not suit to have less than half a denier's space between each thread.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the muscles are stretched by the bones after constriction in their joints, put over them bandages of linen or coarse wool, so they do not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When a wound is bleeding and the joints are broken, I will provide the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not proper to strictly bind all broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limbs are large, it is not proper to tightly bind them for the first few days or even up to seven, or more depending on how serious each abscess that occurs is.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And here is the way of applying old plaster to restore breaks, dislocations, and twists: take some flour that stays on mill walls and mix it with plenty of eggs. Create a paste neither too thin nor too thick, use this application method, which is the common way of applying restorative plaster in various situations, equally suitable for men, women, and children, as it isn't overly harsh or cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way to apply plaster that restores fractures and dislocations: take 3 parts of barley, dahlia, rue, and asafetida, and add gum Arabic and mint, with a total of .x.З.; myrrh and aloes, totaling .v.З.; garlic, in the amount of .viiij. З.; grind these ingredients to make a powder, then mix it thoroughly with eggs; if the consistency of this plaster is warm, use it for treatment, as it has a good composition, quickly sets broken bones right, and is effective on many people.

З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plastering suitable for twists: take mugwort and wild savory, in 10 parts; myrrh and aloes, in 8 parts; cassia, in 6 parts; balm from Armenia, in 10 parts, grind well, mix with water or enough egg white, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another method of dressing joint injuries and exposed bones, to alleviate pain and help heal wounds: take new wool, cook it in fat and oil, then apply it on the wound. These dressings don't fully heal but are better for soothing abscess pain, and properly relieving bone pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of dressing broken bones for healing: take dried fig leaves and terrestrial elm leaves, grind them together, then apply as a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another method for dressing in the restoration of bone fracture and reducing pus discharge. Take root of wild marjoram, chamomile, violet flowers, groundnut flour, each of one part; grind them, mix with wine, and if your limbs are warmed, mix it with moist coriander water, or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another method for dressing better than the first one when pus is being restored within the limb. Take roots of wild marjoram and sesame seeds, balm, melilot, and mint, as well as violet and chamomile flowers, from each take a part; grind them, mix with salt water or sweet water, or wine according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras in his book states that only balm made of beeswax and oil should be applied to the broken limb for restoration purposes, and nothing else. He also indicates it should be between two substances that are neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems like Galen suggests we should apply something to the broken limb for restoration; some things that are dry but a bit warm, such as mirr (myrrh), aloes, and incense, and similar substances, just as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to plaster for injury and pain: take maguey (agave) and wool from human corpses, or bird feathers, and mustard leaves, and equal parts of these, grind them, and make a plaster with them and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then remove a little later, and be careful that the patient does not feel any pain, nor does the bone of its place move; if not removing with hands soon.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes to the limb, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hurry, and remove it, and apply the plaster now; take a light cloth and a wet sponge from the sea, and immerse it in water, and hold over the area until the itching stops and the pain is soothed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the limb rest for an hour, then place it on dry wool, soaked in water or rose oil, and bind it with a cloth until you are sure of removing any pus.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the inflammation and pain in the limb settle, then relieve the discomfort, then continue with gentle re-bandaging, and a little plaster, but do not bind it as tightly as before; proceed with great care until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you notice that pus and redness, pain, swelling are still present everywhere in the area, indicating inflammation, then you need to apply plaster and bandage again, so start doing this as you did before, equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if you don't observe any of the conditions we've mentioned for the limb, or if it doesn't resolve until after three days, four days, five days, seven days; and each time, let it rest for twenty days, according to what is observed, as long as the healing process continues, approaching adjustment with flesh.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Therefore apply the constraint more than initially, and let his flesh grow bigger, as I said before; and if you see that his neck dries out more than it should, know that no improvement can come.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Apply hot water every time you reset the neck, and do this once a day, and loosen the joint a little.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	Through this process, then cut the dislocated limb and treat it immediately as the laymen do, which results in permanently twisting the member back into place: this is harmful, and such treatments are dangerous. I see no other solution than to rest and properly open it.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Through various methods of breaking up
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many methods of fractures exist, and various shapes occur, with their causes being distinguished;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are fractures caused by the impact of a sword, and necks crush all the bone up to the syfac which is below the bone, such as what a hammer or staff does; for this reason, this method of fracture is called 'crushing' or 'smashing'.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or when the sword crushes the bone from above without piercing it, this method of fracture is called 'absolute' fracture; and both large and small wounds result from these two types of fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is sequential impact, or a crack or neck of stone, or through stone, or other similar occurrences.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a break at the bone, which comes up to the membrane beneath the bone, or above it, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there's a wound that reaches into the bone as thin as a hair, and this crack is small, and because of this, it's called this 'hair-like' break;
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is made by striking with a stone or falling, or from some other cause, causing part of the bone to be pushed in and resulting in fractures where the limb ends like candle holders when they crack on the vessels; it happens inside the stone.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more frequently in those with softer bones, such as children's bones;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And occurs in all these ways of breaking where small fragments are extracted as with nuts; and I will speak about it in its proper place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And know all ways of breaking through extraction from them, and investigation with attempts, and through the corrupted matter which is upon them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is known by this: when one has exposed the bone and rubs it together, then the dark fracture opens.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, be vigilant about maladies and if you see no adverse event such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, stretching, swelling, fever ague, and if the eyes emit and turn red or other similar symptoms in various conditions, it cannot be healed without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an alarming occurrence, yet still hope for recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the nose comes to you first, and it's in winter, it is fitting to remove the bone before the fourteenth day after the month you could.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in summer, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the pus under the bone becomes infected, and the accidents we have said occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the bone shatters up to the membrane that covers the brain, it is necessary for you to split the broken part like this: and take hold of the head from the patient's side, and uncover as much as possible on the bone in all ways you can, and more than enough according to the shape of the wound.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And if the flow of blood comes to reveal the bone, or pus pocket, then assist with what is required, and it is that you fill the wound with moist cloths infused in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And let the wound rest until the pus pockets are relieved and there's assurance of blood flow; then begin inside the bone to extract, and this is done according to two methods: one method is that you cut in a narrow incision at the front, and it's the shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another cut of about double the size of the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method involves making various cuts of different sizes, some narrow and others wide, with sharp points, made from iron; and you should do this gently so as not to injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is protruding and hard, it is necessary that you puncture through it internally, in such a way that you administer cuts with needles, not entirely so that they do not pierce beyond the bone's edge, and must have above the point a margin or one circle, which does not let the point pass beyond the bone; and you must have more than this, so that each goes into its place of the thickness of the bone, so that you have needles for all its edges; and this is the form of the three ways of using needles:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing through the bone internally is that you place one needle on the bone, and twist with your fingers until you know that the bone is pierced. Then put the needle elsewhere a little after, and do this all internally. After that, cut out the space between the parts of the bone using the incisors, and do so more finely and gently than possible, as we have said, until you bring the bone to your hand or any tool you have such as forceps, tweezers; and be sure not to touch the brain nor the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and cut the bone, it is necessary that you refine what remains of the bone with all one other tool resembling an incisor, but it must be stronger and more delicate than the other incisors;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And if it stays without any small bones, or no scales, then gently manipulate with two fingers. Then heal the wound with bandages and treatments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of treatment is this which Galen stated, who says it is safer; and he pulls very strongly, and that's his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to uncover part of the bone, where the break opens and moves, so that once you have uncovered that part, you will place under the tip of this oblong incision, which has this form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut from one side only, and make the cut on both sides of the bone, so that when you cut it is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer upwards, so that you gently scrape the entire surface of the bone, and take care not to damage the mesh that's there.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it's close to bone, gently squeeze it, for bone reacts well without harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone break doesn't go through the membrane, and only part of the bone is cut above, with small pieces remaining, after smoothing that area it is necessary to remove the scales using a fine shaver you must have in various quantities. To apply the most suitable for each place according to the work and the shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	When facing large shavers, then proceed to finer ones, and never cease this practice until it's done well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair cutting tasks and subtle breaks, you must adapt according to their direction; and this matter is not resolved for him who has devoted his study to this craft.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the scar is uncovered, it is necessary that you take one linen bandage according to the amount of the wound, and smear with oil of roses, and place it on the wound;
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another bandage doubled up to two or three layers and soak it in wine and oil of roses; place it on the first bandage; do this as gently as you can without burdening the scar, then apply another layer over it, without pulling it too tightly so that it only touches the wound.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	Leave it like this for one or two days until the abscess has subsided, then remove the bandage and administer remedies such as the roots of lavender, flour of myrrh, incense powder, and other similar items; make a powder from these things, apply it to the wound, and then administer further gentle medicines without causing irritation.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And see that the wound is clean immediately, do not leave any pus or allow it to coagulate, because when blood clots on the brain's tissue, it circulates and spreads, causing great mischief to the patient; for when one places something sharp there, it pierces through from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, take heed, if no accidents befall the patient as we have said, if it is doubtful, then there should be no fear.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if the illness does not come from anything that we have applied to him, given its nature of effect, should it be that case you must take a part of honey and three parts of almond oil, mixed with one spoonful of glue, then place this on your wound.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Following are the methods of treatment until it becomes healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that neither of the two neck bones above, or one by itself, should be broken for this reason; they are two bones. The one below is cartilaginous and does not break, even if you try to bend or twist it, and afterwards it heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, you should bend your small finger or part of the neck, and make the same break inside with your index finger, and in front to the side, until the neck revives according to its natural shape;
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	Do this gently, and be sure that the patient does not feel pain through your operation.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part above the nose, and cannot come to his nose, then it's necessary that you place him level with the head of a rod a bit thick.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two parts, then remake it, and hasten to restore the first day, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	But if not, after the seventh or the eighth day, when the abscess has calmed down, then apply a poultice of linen to the head near the nose; if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you apply another poultice on the other side, if the break is there; and let them be large enough to fill the depressions near the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And it is said that one must moisten the tents with butter and change each day. I do not think this is right, but they should be moistened in the preparation of an egg yolk mixture and powdered flour; then let the tent remain until the bone is firm and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one uses goose feathers instead of tents, and if it is one egg's worth of fat in the middle, and the wound heals, and breaths through the patient; then do whatever you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if pus comes out through the nose as you are working, then put moistened lint or cotton in oil mixed with rose water, or a spoonful of almond oil.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if abscesses do not occur, then apply a poultice on the surface, made of sawdust flour and incense powder mixed with beaten egg yolk. Then place light bandages over it but do not tie them tightly.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the fracture is small and broken into many pieces, then use tools suitable for this when extracting them, first cut along the break, and treat things that are in the contaminated flesh, and suture it. Then cover with suitable poultices or ointments.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound within the bone, then treat with lint, until it has healed. Then place on it pieces of plaster, while it is still healing.
de la routure de la mandibule	On the rupture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is broken outwards, and there is no wound outwardly visible, only the break is outwardly present, not being split into two parts externally but cracked internally. If one knows this lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary; if the breakage occurs in the right part, you press your index finger into the mouth near the wound. And if the breakage is in the left mandible, then press your index finger of your right hand, and gently press the break internally, and perform this action with the other hand outwardly, making sure it's even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the breakage of the jawbone is split into two parts, it should be treated with an extension of both hands until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement of the teeth occurs, or a rupture, hold them with a thread made of gold, silver or silk. Then place on the broken mandible wax, and place underneath two double cloths; then place on one cloth a large triangle well made, or an equal piece of leather long and wide according to the mandible's size. Tie it in place as much as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and have them eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you notice that the figure changes, release it on the third day and then reposition what has become distorted; apply plaster with some powder from a mill mixed with plenty of egg or saffron flour after removing the wax; place wool under the plaster for warmth, and if the plaster hardens and the patient's position does not change, let them remain like that until they heal; many recover in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if it comes to incision at the foot, then apply what we have instructed many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is both fracture and wound together, reward is null for any bone fragment that has been removed; such subtlety of extracting requires instruments suitable for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, enlarge it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and there remains none, if the wound is wide, place one poultice suitable for this over it to encourage flesh growth until healing occurs.
de la forcele	by the strength
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The force breaks multiple times in front of the shoulder, towards it, and the breaking occurs in three ways: or it is broken and severed in two parts, with pieces present, and it is easier to restore; or there is a break accompanied by injury.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And for the procedures when the break is due to injury, have two ministers, so that one examines the shoulder where the force has broken; and the other extends the neck towards the part. Then set the break equal with your hands, so that its form be as it should, and let not any appearance or movement be seen.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place a round sponge of cloth or wool under the shoulder towards the leg; make its size according to your needs. Stretch and lift the broken force, hold the sponge in your hand so that you can set the break equal, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the force to the outside due to it coming forwards, then the patient should lie with their head on their shoulder blade, and place a pillow under one shoulder. Sometimes only one of the large fosciles breaks, or sometimes the smaller one does, and occasionally they both break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small bones break, the treatment is light, both for restoration and healing; and when the large ones break, the healing process is poor, it's worse than if they broke together. If it's only the small bone that breaks, then it's sufficient to gently extend it a bit and make it even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it's the large bone that breaks, you should strain harder; and place him on one cushion, and raise the hand of his side higher than the others, and make each finger lower than their counterparts, and have the patient cross their fingers with themselves, and another cushion in front slightly higher to prevent any discomfort. Then extend both the doctor's arms towards the elbow part beneath their hands, or at a single elbow point, and one assistant at a single point above. And then place them even, according to their best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the breaking into pieces, you place each piece in its own place, and if there is none of them that holds onto his sense, and you cannot restore it to its place, then cut on top of and through the bone, as we said previously.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the wounding in an injury, I spoke about it in the singular chapter; then take care of the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if during the beginning of the restoration, abscesses appear, then apply a dressing.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if any bad incidents happen to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, it is necessary that you immerse the limb in hot water until that itch is relieved; and let the limb not be allowed to rest. And then resume tightening, and once the ligament has been severed and the bone exposed, and similar actions have occurred, guide them accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if precautions are taken so that no injuries can come to the limb because it is too constricted, it is necessary to soften it with heat for a short time and leave it like this for several days until the pains disappear, and then you restrain.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of the things we have said come to pass in the patient, or if he is not cured after twenty days, then allow him to move his hands towards his neck, and make sure that his neck muscles are evenly aligned, while taking care to avoid movement and digestion, and sleep on his back; know that this healing process takes place in thirty days or thirty-five, and by chance in twenty, depending on the compositions and the nature of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	Of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	You know that on the back of the hand and with us the bones suffer little breaks, and no more than bend many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the heel of the hand is broken or bent, it is necessary that the muscles heal in line and straight ahead just as they are; then place your hand on the stretched bed, and stretch out the fingers of the broken bones, and place them evenly under the eyes, until they are well joined; and apply the plaster and bandages, if there are no abscesses, then put an awl according to the size of the limb; and wrap it in one strip of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is in the webbing between the toes near the belly of the hand, make a roll of linen cloth, and instruct the patient to place it on their broken toe; then stretch it with a long strip of linen, and position the awl as large as the hand's heel, stretching it accordingly.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is at the front, it should be that you place a splint above and another underneath in the foot part, so that your hand is opened and straight, then bind them entirely around the hand, and seal off the connection between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the break occurs at any of the feet of the fingers, it's if they are splayed, as it should be; and you hold them with the foot, and if you see fit to place a small straight splint for lifting the breakage, and not let it move; and if the break is on other fingers, like in the index or among others, treat them equally, and bind with the healthy finger that follows; or you bind all together, so that nothing moves, or you set it on a splint, as when you hold up; take care in the restoration and arrangement of each abscess, and prepare for what comes to you, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bone of the knee is often broken, and one can see it when it turns frontwards and backwards; and its repair consists in .i., tying above the breakage, and .i. another below it.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the glands lie on her face, then extend each minister his link to its equal part; and this is when the break is within the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the break is close to the root of the knee, then have one link towards the foot and the other links below the break. And similarly if it is close to the elbow, then place the ligaments behind the elbow, and thus apply the plaster from above; then put the bone into its place equally with its two hands, as long as it follows its natural shape, and then apply the plaster and the bandage, and if no abscesses come about.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is pus at the site, let it heal then return to your work and treatment; the wound is made in such manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap over the burn. I. e., bandage it with two or three layers of a thick material, leaving excess aside. Then place your leg until the heel reaches the ankle bone, and insert one long thread between the calf and leg, under the knee downwards, then lead the thread to the top above; after that wrap the bandage around both the leg and the calf, then put a stone on top of the burn wound, and place a stone over the bone of the leg. Then insert the remaining length of material under the calf and the leg with the sole facing upwards for equal pressure. Begin to wrap tightly in three or four rounds around the burn; when going beyond the burn area, do so with less tightness; then take two threads that you have inserted between the leg and calf, bind them with three stones placed above each other, after which return under the thread as far as you can go underneath the foot; and then tighten it, until it doesn't move from its place, then leave it like this until no further pus, inflammation or similar symptoms appear.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens that the bones are dislocated, you should reassemble them in their correct position as we have mentioned many times; and if there are pieces of bone that are displaced, they must be treated accordingly if possible; and if not, it is necessary to cut through the tissue and draw out the bone; then treat it according to what we have said until it heals.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And no time is broken the egg until these are put in, such as in the shoulder and at the elbow; however, when restoration is made this way, there is no pain to the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	Know that the egg is restored in one day, or somewhat less, or somewhat more, depending on the diversity of body types.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the garden alley
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that in the garden alley there is little breaking, but it bends many times. And if it breaks, it's usually just a crack or two small fragments, and occurs with or without injuries, and one feels this well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez. de la brisure de la jambe	of the breaking of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	You know that in the leg there are two bones. The one is named straight by right - "hammers" and the other is called "shinbone"; and every kind of injury or breakage can occur just as it does with an arm, and for this reason the process of restoration is done similarly to that of an arm, and the operations are all the same.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if the two bones are broken together, then turn the leg from all sides.

Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. And if the large bones are broken, one feels great pain and sees it clearly; then turn sideways. And when you have completed your work, take two sticks of wood that will support the leg on both sides, and they should be as long as from the knee to below. Then wrap around them with two lengths of leather, and tie in the middle so the leg cannot lean to either side; thus it is well done. And no one should administer a splint longer than the leg, made of wood, and place this on the leg to prevent movement; do this directly where there was an injury; and move the leg each day to check for pus or any other complications; heal as long as you are able.
de la brisure des os dou piet	From the breaking of bones due to injury
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	Ankle injuries do not come from breaking bones, but rather due to certain positions that the feet can be in, and there is only strength when in multiple dispositions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier. de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	regarding the breaking of the bone in the hand
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of her nature is broken, if it makes itself to swell, then lean her toward the lower part of her back, and hold her behind. Then fill the hole that was made by nature with cotton, and also put in as much as one egg; then turn out the woman, and lift her back slowly and slowly, and then let the cotton jump until it reaches the entrance of nature, and brings the bone along with it; and when she wants to urinate, take out the cotton, and once she has urinated, put her back again, do this for seven days or a bit more: thus will the break be healed. If you see, take a goat's bladder, tie a stick at one end of it, fill the bladder entirely in nature; then inflate it forcefully using the stick until the bladder is full inside: nature will heal the break. Then fill it with cotton and leave it like this for some days, till it is healed over.

de brisure avec plaie	Of breaking with injury
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a break with an injury, even if it's large, as with bones of the wrist or shoulder blade or similar, that they be now treated, so that the treatments we have mentioned testify to.

And if the wound has healed, you should reapply vinegar, and if there's no other remedy, then start restoring the break in the same hour or day. If abscesses occur, apply them immediately.

Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone is broken and visible through the uncovered thigh, it must be gently placed with your hands, in a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions are not yet equipped for your hands to make them even, take this iron tool you have, which is .vij. or .viij. inches long, and its width should correspond to the size of the wound; and it's necessary for the surgeon to grip around .iii. or iiij., according to what he needs for each treatment of a broken bone; and may be round and somewhat thick, so that it does not bend under compression against your limb during operation, and have sharp points ahead, and thick at the middle in front, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.
