And it is called "palainche" because the curved ends should be placed on the visible part of the bone; and strike once, until they return, and ensure that they are even against each other. And if the breakage is subtle, and the instruments cannot properly grasp the bone, then you must hold the tip of the bone as long as the instruments have control.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot return the bone back, as we have said, if you have an appropriate tool for this purpose, such as a scalpel or a knife, at your power; then cut the one that is stuck in the bone with hardness and small shavings.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone is returned, and if there's great pain afterwards in the limbs, know that it hasn't been placed naturally. Do as much as to place it correctly, then moisten with one part of a black wine stiptic, and properly if it has healed; and don't put any ointment or other thing on the wound when there's an open sore, so that no infection or corruption occurs; then apply these remedies after you've restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover it entirely according to the size of the wound, and be well aware not to restrain the wound with pressure; many times people have done this and brought about death or corrosion in the patient; and let your handings be softer than usual, as they do with other injuries.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is bad or large and you suspect that harmful occurrences might have happened there, just like we've said before, and pain is felt in the limb, then it's not fit to apply remedies; but cover it completely instead of applying them. And when after one or two days you see a boil form on the wound, remove whatever you placed over it entirely with wine, and apply a healing ointment for wounds, like a tetrachemical ointment, and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must dislocate the limb twice a day, in the morning and at vespers, until it is united and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it should be that the limbs are placed so that the wound heals in such a way that the bone comes together lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the days pass and it cannot heal otherwise than at once with the bone, know that there are small fragments of bone, which is why you should work on the wound with traction, and remove all these unnecessary pieces that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if a fistula forms in the wound or there is another form of corruption, you must treat it according to what he instructed before in this chapter. And when the bone breaks and opens on the limb, such as in the bone of the foot or shoulder, or other similar large limbs, do not attempt treatment because many times death ensues from it; however, let it heal by itself until it discharges pus after about 20 or 30 days, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it alone.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The blows that come from sweat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come across various effects after the healing of injuries due to the breeze. Indeed, it is something to see how the limb's shape changes; and by chance, cannot perform its natural tasks on the limb.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then in dealing with these things: if they are inflamed due to heat or cold, administer stictic medicines like aloes, frankincense, myrrh, sarsaparilla, senna, and similar others, as you see fit among any of these substances, or all together, and mix them with stictic wine or with plenty of eggs or with garlic; and apply them to the wound in poultices, pressing it well, but not letting it move in your hands during the day; then remove it, and repeat another one until the pus is extracted; or you can apply on a well-made piece of plaster; for the properties of plaster are that it removes all swellings from the limbs; and if the pus has hardened like stone, so it needs to be removed, then scrape off any excess above it, and leave the treatment as long as it heals.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The limb that is weak after a siege
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the breaking of the bone is restored, and after that the limbs are weak and subtle, it happens for many reasons: due to one factor being that they were tied too tightly, not as they should have been; or because there were too many bands, not allowing normal circulation in the limb; or because of an excess of swelling; or due to too large movements at inappropriate times; or because they have little blood in their body, making them weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment involves making the patient eat well, and make the body tender until the pulse grows in him; then give them baths, and bring him joy and comfort. Afterwards apply ointment to the limb so that the ointment attracts to the large swelling, and cleanse it with water often, until the swelling corresponds to the limb; and restore its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	If the member is twisted after recovery.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are twisted after restoration, and if the bones are broken apart, while the shape of the body is ugly afterwards, it does not lose its natural function: nor should you believe those who say one must break the limb anew; many people do this in our land; these operations are criticized and cause great harm, even to the point of death. However, if the bruises and injuries are fresh, then they should be treated with hot water or softifying herbs, like leaves from valerian, roots, and thyme, among others; and apply a poultice made from them; you can also take fat figs, grind them with flour from rye, and similar medicines that reduce inflammation. And make an ointment for poultices, as properly done salve, and take valerian root, mix it with grease from lard or oil of safflower, and apply this as a poultice; alternatively, you can take fat figs, grind them with rye flour, and similar remedies that reduce swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And each time the joint is dislocated, it should be treated by rubbing continuously and for a long period with wet hands. And let there be one movement of the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is old and hardened, like bone, and needs to be removed with the iron, if it suits one must cut up until reaching the bone, with a slight, gentle incision. And apply concentration and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, because it cannot move then, and the limb is misaligned, causing great pain and injury to the patient.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation affects none, if it suits now to bring back without hesitation.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if one delays, the limbs swell up, and by chance should it be necessary to reset them at their current location; for this does not suit when trying to move them while they are swollen: many times it brings on pus and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	If this happens, instruct the patient's attendant to heal them first, allowing until all abscesses subside; then immerse the limb in hot water and oil, gently reposition it, and treat each part as their treatment would come naturally to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on shoulder dislocations up to this point.
des mandibules	of the jaw
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It happens that the jaws are dislocated downwards, and the dislocations of both occur in two ways: either they are somewhat bony at their roots and slightly softened; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards the chin, and expel saliva from the mouth so that one cannot hold it, nor close their mouth, and wrap their tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When a dislocation is small, it can return through various positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it's complete and fully occurred, you should reset it quickly without hesitation.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And in such a way that the surgeons cut near to where the hair grows, and place their thumbs under the root of the jaw dislocation within the mouth; if the dislocation is at two inches, one hand should be inside while the other remains outside for balance; command the patient to soften his jaws and move them around.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And hold the thumbs in place until they settle back into position.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if bringing them back causes pain, especially when the two jaws are together, so that the heads of bones from hot water and oil, as long as they are gently brought back; do not overly force it to bring back, as we have said.

et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	And let the patient sleep on their back, and keep the head between two cushions, so that it doesn't move neither to the right nor to the left, nor strain itself in any way. And then taste this to be lightly lifted, and does not struggle with opening the mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw is well set and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be placed in their proper position within an hour, and are not returned to them, it leads to fevers that become habitual, and at times abdominal pain, and at times vomiting of clear contents.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is loss; and many times, death has befallen those to whom it happens, within eight days.
de la forcelle	from the forceful (context unclear without more information)
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forces cannot relieve the pain from within the body's continuity or from its backside; it can only be relieved once outside, and this is clearly felt.

de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: of which one occurs when it dislocates from the part of the scapula downwards; and the second is at the part under the heel; and by chance dislocates from the upper part, which happens rarely;
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	And it never dislocates behind the shoulder or inside the nerves; and often dislocates downwards towards the scapula, even for those with little flesh, because in these cases it jumps quickly; for those with enough flesh, it jumps to points and returns to them.

Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you must verify it as long as you are certain; then you may begin treatment.

et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	You will find a hollow at the top of the shoulder. puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then bandage the patient's back, and place a flat piece of wool under their armpit, neither too soft nor too hard. et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	And another minister cuts the neck of the patient, so that it doesn't move down; this shoulder comes back right now, and if you see to reset it according to this manner:

et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And other ministers pull the hand from the injury downwards towards the belly. And if the injured area is too light, support him with something heavy, and the dislocation comes back now.

et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	and if she does not want to return with all these things that we have said, then do this treatment: take one leg of .ij. arms and .iiij. sticks that are broad, which should be able to enter quite smoothly on the side opposite the dislocation, according to this shape:

And let your hands remain like this.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	It should be that he eats little, until the limbs are strengthened, because it will heal faster; and then eat more after five days or seven, and move it; and if it is firm and it is not softened, it will be healed.

And if you do all this, and it dislocates after seven days, and the joint doesn't hold, and cannot lift your arm up, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or extended or weakened; and know that the joint would never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocation near the buttocks, and breasts, or behind, is caused by pushing, extension of hands, and administration in another place; treatment should be applied as long as it's clean.

And if after the healing comes redness to the limb, and delayed movements, then immerse the patient in hot baths many times, until that redness is alleviated, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the shoulder joint issue
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated at points, and it returns to those points; if it has been dislocated from all sides, as well in front and behind, and dislocation does not respond because you can see it clearly and feel it clearly; and it is dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And when you unite the arm bone with the good side, if you can see it clearly. Because the joint is bony, and cannot bend the arm or touch its shoulder to any extent.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you should reset it this way that the abscesses are closed, for if they were to be left open, there would be trouble in closing them; and sometimes it cannot be brought back completely, especially when it's at the back; it is worse than other dislocations and causes more pain, and by chance it brings death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And restoration occurs like this when you can bring it back: extend their hand with both of your hands; and their arms are spread out, and the hands face towards the body along the length of the forearm, in and out, and hold the joint at its natural place or at the base of the palm, until they return to their original position.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And when it comes to dislocation in front of the body, it returns as soon as he doubles his hand on his own and holds the joint at the base of the palm with a tool that is set back.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it does not wish to return to its place, administer strong extension; and when both hands extend the arm, and bend them both, so that they do not move during the extension. Then turn the arm in each part, then once you have wrapped a double length of cloth long and wide;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	And when you grasp the joint with your hand, if you apply some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint back into place until it heals;
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And when it's at its place, place dry plaster with an egg yolk on it, push it back into place firmly, and let the arm hang down by the side of the body for some days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in its place, release the ligament and let it be; and if you see that the joint does not sit well, redo the plastering and the bandage, and let them stay like that for some more days until it is firmly set; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	And if it feels sore after the return of the joint and it moves again, wash and rub it nicely, pressing until it is relieved; or you can place a layer of fatty mutton fat on the joint, then leave it for one day and one night, then re-apply heat, and let it enter or take a bath.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And when it sweats, you should rub the joint gently, then place the bone back, and then immerse it in water; and do this twice or three times until it heals; and if possible, apply moist cow's fat mixed with butter on it and keep it there; if it works, it will return to its proper position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The hand dislocation has occurred and the recovery is faster than for other joints, throughout the body. It's necessary to return it to its place as soon as possible, while it's still dislocated, so that the fingers swell or an abscess forms.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the process is as follows: you place your hand on a table and extend the minister's hand, then inspect it by making it equal, so that they position their palm against the appearance of the joint, and hold it until it returns to its original position.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	In every case, it is necessary to ensure that they look at whether it is in place; therefore, have the patient place the back of their hand on a table during extension and retraction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele aparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, have the patient place the back of their hand on the table, and inspect by placing their hand against the appearance of the joint. If it returns to this position now, then it is correctly aligned.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, if you hold back with soothing plaster applications, and leave it there without needing to start over.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if they cannot bear it, and you can't put it back in place after some days, if the joint remains twisted;
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And it doesn't harm the patient so long as their hands are in plaster, and they can't apply any force at all: then you'll know that a nerve has been cut, or an artery; if there's no other way to relieve pain than with fire cautery, and by chance there isn't anything else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hands are in plaster, apply what we have said on plaster, then apply it and leave them for five days, then remove it and leave them as is.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is no pain, if the water is warm, and rub it until it becomes clean.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Regarding the dislocation of the fingers of the hand.
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	The fingers of the hand are never dislocated from each other, neither at the back of the palm nor at the belly.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Therefore keep the fingers intact, and prevent the dislocation from spreading to his pockets until it recovers. Then support the head of the fingers, and bend it towards the part that is separated;
et le laisse .ij. jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit,	And let it be for two days, and then make him equal on that day; and without tie him up, as we have said, and loosen him each day, and make him move, and bind him again at night; and do this often until he becomes constricted.
et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	And do it in the same way, if it is dislocated in the belly of the hand, and do as you did before until it heals; and do it similarly, when it is dislocated on another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Dislocation of the ankle, dislocation of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When it is dislocated in the back or neck, or when there are multiple dislocations, if no cure is applied, because time rushes the patient into harm.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les .ij. cuixes ou li dui bras ou .j.	And the symptoms are that the evacuations start suddenly and against one's will, not being able to hold them, and many times various parts of the body, or both hands, or either arm, or one foot become weak.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a iiij. pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	And many times the calf muscle splits into four parts; that which becomes stiff at the back is called 'gibbous'.
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	The treatment is to reward if this 'gibbous' has come from childhood: without any treatment or healing until then.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And the one that comes from falling, impacts or similar things, according to old curing methods with big words, it did not bring any great benefit in all.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	But I have shortened it according to my intention, and formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the illness coming before the belly, none has health or strength;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en .ij. costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	And also that which comes straight to the two ribs, and cannot cure from anything else than what directly affects the back, as I say;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en .i. leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	And it is that if the disease spreads across his flank in one length equally and has strain under him, so that he does not get wounded;
puis fiche .i. tison au chief en terre forment, et .i. autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et .i. autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	Then place a coal in the ground at the head and one more on the feet, and tie with a bandage around the armpits near the hair, and another by the hips, and knees, and ankles;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les .ij. tisons;	and two people hold the bandages in place, one at the head and the others on the feet, between the two coals;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and make sure they are well closed, the coal as we have said, and she should place her palms on the back until she regains consciousness.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de .iij. bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if this cure doesn't revive her, take a board of three arms long and place it over the back, and if she's on her side, position the head at one end of the board over the back. Then put the center of the board under the spine;
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	Place the eyes of his feet onto the other head of the table, and press firmly, until he regains consciousness in its place; and if you can see, perform it on the wrist that turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches .ij. tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez .ij. autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And when you place two pieces of charcoal on the head of the leg from one arm across, and towards the feet of another, with each piece of charcoal, put in between them an arm's length of space.
et ait en chescun tison .i. pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns .ij. tisons ait .i. tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en .ij. tornans .ij. petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	Place one piece of charcoal (or the part that turns) on each coal, or where the wrist turns, and ensure the coals are firmly in the ground so they don't move; between the two coals place a turning coal, where it turns, and between the two turning ones have two small pieces of charcoal of an arm's length for turning the wrist.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And then secure the first ligament between the elbows and head, and the second ligament towards the feet at the other elbow, and each servant turns their elbow to all the ligament, and the masters place the spine evenly as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de .iij. dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when they are even, place a desiccative plaster with plenty of egg on it and then coat it, then cover it with a tablet of three inches long, which makes the area of the boil and the healthy part of the spine visible. Then secure it with a ligament as we have said, use the patient's natural sweating process until it is healed;
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc,	And if anything comes at the end of healing, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines with the decoction that we have said earlier. And every time you administer one piece of plumb.
et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And sometimes there appears the appearance at the bottom spinal bone of the back, and one should consider that it is a dislocation; and it is the bone that opens, for which reason we must not have any assumption: an accident might bring about death.
des dislocations de la hainche	dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and shoulder only suffer dislocations, unlike other joints; and the hip joint is dislocated according to four parts: internally and externally, in front and behind; and more internally elsewhere, and less dislocated in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of its dislocation internally is that when one joins the diseased leg with the healthy one, it becomes longer, and the diseased knee opens more than the healthy one, and the diseased knee cannot bend to touch the fire;
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And it is when the limbs are swollen due to an abscess, because the shoulder comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him who approaches death, so it is that this event is contrary to what was before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him who is coming towards death are such that his leg is well according to its fulfillment; still though, he does not double bend his knee without pain, and if you try to make him walk, he cannot move forward and retains his urine, and swells at his ankle, and when he walks, he steps on his heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who is behind are such that he cannot spread his knee or double it, and that leg is more curved than the other, and his ankle is flattened, and that shoulder comes up under his back.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The correction of this semblance of dislocation involves you rewarding it if the dislocation is old and remains according to its position, without any treatment needed; and there should be no assumption about it.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for those whose dislocation is recent, and there are four ways of dislocation, if you act quickly to restore the joint, and stretch it inwards and outwards, and move it towards the right and left; perhaps if it returns on its own and no further treatment is needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles .i. ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a .ij. mains, ou a .i. liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it doesn't return in this manner, then you should apply strong remedies, and hold the leg strongly with both hands or around one knee where it is tied to the thigh;
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and apply other remedies while holding his hand above in such a way that he extends his hands beyond his knees, then he forces the body with one blow of force against the calf; and another holds the head at the strap.
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And extend both upwards and downwards at once, until the patient lifts off the ground in one movement, and stays hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is typical for four similar situations, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it's correct.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	But if it's not like that, then treat according to its appearance. When dislocations are in the pantedens (chest), you should have the patient lie on their healthy side and secure them at the root of the arm, then place the head over the armpit, extend the bandage towards the throat and against force;
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	Then take another assistant to hold the patient's arms, and wrap around the fleshy part of the diseased arm, stretching it upwards in this formation: if it returns to its original position now; and this method of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les .ij. piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les .ij. talons, et sus les .ij. genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue .ij. dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot squeeze it this way as we have said, then you must tie the two feet of the afflicted side together with a strong bandage below both the heels and above both knees, and ensure that the diseased leg extends an inch more than the other;
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre .ij. bras de lonc; puis comande a .j. ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then have it suspended from the head of a post, and let it be two arms' length above the ground; then instruct one minister to embrace the head of the leg, and have another ministers hanging with the afflicted side, who should embrace around the leg forming it into place, as now the joint is coming back quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne .i. liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is at front, if you place the afflicted side as we have said in those with agility and strength, and pull one bandage properly on the diseased leg and also around the foot.
puis met .ij. tisons, .i. au chief et .i. autre as piez, puis fiche .i. tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	Then put two needles, one on the head and the other in the armpit, then insert a needle between the thighs of the patient in their shape.
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and place wet cloths around them, so the patient doesn't blister, then extend each limb towards themselves, and set their dislocated hand in line with their body.
S’elle revient, c’est boin. Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it returns to its place, that's good. If not, put them on a table and press them like we have instructed in the dislocation of the shoulder blade, then lie the patient down on their healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it should be extended as quickly as possible, following what I have said; and place their suffering limb on the back of their shoulder blade, then press with the other hand, and extend it downwards towards their knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les .ij. hainches;	And if the dislocation is at the back, it does not require extending the body backwards or lifting up from the ground, rather it should be placed in the same position as when the hip was dislocated behind, just like we have said about lying on both hips.
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	And if it's in the face, and the neck is stretched as we've said before, and pressure should be applied at the joint on the table;
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	And it will be right when the limbs extend their legs and they are equal; then adjust the thighs, and apply the plaster, and strain with a bandage, so that the hip doesn't move;
et se repose .iij. jors ou .iiij., puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse. iij. jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And let it rest for three or four days, then release and apply the plaster; and if you see that they are equal, strain again as before, and leave them for three more days; then release and allow them to move fully until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The shoulder joint can be dislocated in three ways: one should know that it can dislocate internally and externally, and behind; and does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the signs for this are that you instruct the patient to bend their leg at their knee, and if they cannot straighten it at their knee, know that they have dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	And the restoration of all this is that you have the patient sit straight, and if they can extend their leg, place your back on their buttocks, and put their foot on your feet;
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les .ij. costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	Then take his knee in your hands and pull it between your fingers. Then bend the two knees gently, forming the shape of the knee. And have other attendants extend his foot as far as possible until the knee returns to its place and there are signs that he has correctly placed his leg slightly below the thigh.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort .iij. jors ou iiij., puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And place the dressing on it, and have him stretch his leg to the thigh, then firmly unite them for three or four days. Then let him rest; and do not move any of the limbs until they are strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the limbs are not yet ready, administer strong extension exercises, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until they recover strength.
de la dislocation dou talon	On the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are never perfectly reduced or completely dislocated, both inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs for this are that the ankle is swollen, and it tries to move towards the part where it has been dislocated:
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	The reduction is gentle, and one should slightly extend it with their hands only when the heel is reduced.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne .i. ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is dislocated completely, it must be that you make the patient stand straight, and hold him two assistants off by his leg, above the ankle;
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre .ij. fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then twice with the left, then lift him up, and firmly push the foot upwards;
et fai ce .ij. fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	and do this twice, as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is well; if not, start over with the process, for it will return.
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche .i. passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it cannot return like that, then have the patient lie down on his back on the ground, and place two stones firmly in the earth between his buttocks, and tie cloths around him so he does not hurt the patient.
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a .i. liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	Then the surgeons cleanse the wound, and some other surgeons stretch his feet or at two inches to the leg bone, so that they lie on the neck of the leg bone;
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	Then each surgeon stretches them equally, and the ladle shall always be placed between the thighs of the patient to hold the limb when it is stretched.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	Then place the mirrors equally at the point of dislocation with both hands, and another surgeon cuts the healthy leg above it, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is at the right position, apply the plaster and put the bandage on top, then tighten it properly, bind the leg to the body, and watch the nerves that are behind the ankle so that the bandage is not too tight.
puis le laisse .ij. jors ou .iij., et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par .iiij. jors;	Then leave it for two or three days, and if they relax, pull them out; then release it on the third day or fourth, and let the patient walk around for four more days;
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And if it goes beyond that point, it is not safe that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses are pressing on him and it comes to this, you must soothe him, as we have said elsewhere, until he feels better.
des dois	Of the fire cautery, command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the arms are dislocated, if they need to be properly stretched as part of their work, it is a simple matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus .i. leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocations are in no bone of the back or foot, it is necessary that you make the patient lie on their full length or on a table entirely straight, and place your foot where it opens from these joints, then press with your foot firmly until they come to themselves.
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a .ij. chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse .iij. jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when they are even and do not open anything, place under the foot of each pig a table with two heads, then hold them in shape, and let them for three days, then release it; and make it rest until it is well healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	regarding wound care and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound accompanies a dislocation, and one seeks to restore it, many times the patient has died:
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	if you are not presumptuous in the treatment, and if you are knowledgeable in the art and have practiced it for a long time, and if you are compassionate and merciful but also patient, do not be rash.
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	And at first apply soothing remedies to the abscesses with cautery, and let the patient remain in God's hands, if you do not see hope of healing;
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	And when you see hope, then reset the limb into its place immediately, so that the abscesses stick and heal.
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	And when the limb is in its place, apply soothing remedies to the abscesses and treat the wound as it should be done, using dried ointments.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	And if there is a break with dislocation and small bones are exposed, set the bones, and do as we have said for simple diseases.
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Amen	And guard yourself against the path of fear, according to what I've said, for this is your duty as per your Creator, and through knowledge arm yourself and know your body. Amen
Explicit le romen de fisique	End the discourse on physicality.
